801 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Fleming v. State of California


No. B074475.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


34 Cal. App. 4th 1378; 41 Cal. Rptr. 2d 63; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 441; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3528; 95 Daily Journal DAR 6063



May 10, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. BC043375, Michael Berg, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, personal representative and family of deceased, appealed an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which sustained a demurrer by defendants, state and state parole officer, on grounds of immunity and dismissed plaintiff's action against defendants which alleged defendants' failure to prevent the murder of deceased by a parolee.


OVERVIEW: A prisoner with a history of pedophilia, violence, and drug abuse was paroled on conditions that he not leave the state and that he not be alone with children. The parolee violated both of these terms, however defendants, state and state parole officer, did not take steps to arrest parolee upon his return. Parolee then left the state again, and kidnapped, tortured, raped and killed decedent in Arizona. Plaintiffs, personal representative and family of decedent, filed an action against defendants for failure to prevent the murder and a civil rights claim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The trial court sustained the demurrers of defendants, and dismissed the action based on grounds of immunity. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court found that defendants were immune from liability under Cal. Gov't Code § 845.8, and that there was no mandatory duty imposed on defendant to arrest parolee which would provide the basis for civil liability. The court rejected plaintiff's arguments that Arizona law should have applied because the actions of defendants occurred in California; and that plaintiffs were deprived of due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court which sustained demurrer by defendants, state and state parole officer, in an action by plaintiffs, personal representative and family of deceased, which alleged defendants' failure to prevent the murder of decedent by a parolee because defendants were immune from liability under statute, the trial court properly applied California law, and plaintiffs' due process rights were not violated.

 

802 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Lopez v. Tulare Joint Union High School Dist.


No. F019400.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


34 Cal. App. 4th 1302; 40 Cal. Rptr. 2d 762; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 428; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3489; 95 Daily Journal DAR 5995



May 9, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified June 8, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Tulare County, No. 153653, Kenneth E. Conn and Gerald F. Sevier, Judges.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. Costs on appeal are awarded to respondents.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant students sought review of a grant of summary judgment in favor of respondent school board officials in appellants' action to prohibit respondents from censoring their video made for a high school film arts class. Appellants asserted that respondents were prohibited from censoring the student-authored work under Cal. Educ. Code § 48907 and Cal. Const. art. I, § 2, which protected students' rights to free expression.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed a grant of summary judgment in favor of respondent school board officials in an action brought by appellant students for a declaratory judgment that respondents were prohibited from censoring or restricting the release of a video made in connection with a film arts class. The video depicted the story of teenage parents and contained profanity and explicit reference to sexual activity. The court rejected appellants' argument that respondents were precluded by Cal. Educ. Code § 48907 and Cal. Const. art. I, § 2, which provided protections for students' free expression rights, from requiring appellants to delete the profanity. The court held that the video was an official student publication and that respondents could restrain such expression because it violated the professional standards of English and journalism provisions of § 48907. The court found that the statute, which permitted prior restraints of profane student expression in official student publications, was a valid time, place or manner restriction when respondents asserted a compelling state interest in promoting moral improvement and regulations were narrowly tailored to meet that interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of respondent school board officials. The court held that respondents had the right to restrain appellant students' use of profanity in the video because it violated the professional journalism standards provisions of the statute. The statute was a valid time, place, and manner restriction on free expression that was narrowly tailored to promote a compelling state interest.

 

803 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Fadelli Concrete Pumping, Inc. v. Appellate Department


No. H012900, No. H012881.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


34 Cal. App. 4th 1194; 40 Cal. Rptr. 2d 757; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 422; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3366; 95 Daily Journal DAR 5742



May 4, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Municipal Court for the Santa Clara Judicial District of Santa Clara County, No. H1092094, Harold L. Cole, Judge. * 


* Commissioner of the Municipal Court for the Santa Clara Judicial District sitting under assignment by the Chairperson of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: For the reasons stated above, defendant's motion to dismiss the appeal is granted. Defendant's petition for certiorari to the Supreme Court is dismissed as moot. Defendant's motion for sanctions is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the People, sought review of the order of the Municipal Court for the Santa Clara Judicial District of Santa Clara County (California) which convicted defendant for violating Cal. Veh. Code § 35551 and imposed a fine that was allegedly too low.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of violating Cal. Veh. Code § 35551, which prohibited the operation of a vehicle over certain statutory weight limits without a permit. The lower court imposed a fine of $ 482. Plaintiff, the People, appealed, claiming that the applicable fine should have been in excess of $ 22,000. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss and a motion for sanctions. The court affirmed and granted defendant's motion to dismiss, holding that plaintiff could not challenge the allegedly unauthorized sentence imposed by the lower court in a misdemeanor case, either by appeal or by extraordinary writ. The judgment was not appealable unless the appeal was authorized by statute, and it did not become appealable merely because it was erroneous. The mere existence of any order after judgment did not make the underlying judgment necessarily appealable. The court determined that plaintiff could not circumvent the limitation on appeals by seeking review by extraordinary writ. The situation of the lower court allegedly miscalculating the fine was not likely to reoccur nor was it of such importance to be considered an extraordinary writ. Sanctions for a frivolous appeal were not warranted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order, holding that plaintiff, the People, did not have statutory authority to challenge, either by appeal or extraordinary writ, an unauthorized sentence for misdemeanor, imposed by the lower court upon defendant. Defendant's motion to dismiss was granted, and motion for sanctions was not warranted.

 

804 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


Superior Court v. County of Mendocino


No. A065039.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


43 Cal. App. 4th 1488; 40 Cal. Rptr. 2d 374; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 401; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3246; 95 Daily Journal DAR 5534



April 27, 1995, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted July 27, 1995 (S046963), Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 4753.
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court. (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cite 34 Cal. App. 4th 679 and 39 Cal. App. 4th 391.)] (See 13 Cal. 4th 45.)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Mendocino County, No. 68620, John K. Letton, Judge. * 


* Judge of the Trinity Superior Court sitting under assignment by the Chairperson of the Judicial Council.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant superior court challenged an order from the Superior Court of Mendocino County (California) that denied its petition for writ of mandate to direct respondent county board of supervisors to provide funding for the salaries of court employees on designated furlough days and to modify the furlough programs to exclude court employees based on Cal. Gov't Code § 68108.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Cal. Gov't Code § 68108, respondent county board of supervisors informed appellant superior court that the courts were to be closed on certain days to effect unpaid work furlough days authorized by respondent's agreement with county employees, but appellant issued orders commanding respondent to provide funding for the salaries of court employees on designated furlough days and to modify the furlough programs to exclude court employees. When respondent failed to honor its orders, appellant petitioned for a writ of mandate, which was denied. On appeal, the court vacated that order and ordered the trial court to issue the writ of mandate, holding that Cal. Gov't Code § 68108 was unconstitutional. The court found that the words of the statute clearly and unequivocally granted respondent the right to close the courts on furlough days except when the presiding judge declared a judicial emergency. This power was unconstitutional because it authorized legislative exercise of powers reserved to the judiciary in matters that impaired the efficient exercise of the judicial function.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's order denying appellant superior court's petition for writ of mandate to direct respondent county board of supervisors to provide funding for court employees on designated furlough days and to modify the furlough programs to exclude court employees because the California statute authorizing respondent's action was unconstitutional. The court ordered the trial court to issue the requested writ of mandate.

 

805 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



In re Shawnn F.


No. F021139.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


34 Cal. App. 4th 184; 40 Cal. Rptr. 2d 263; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 383; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3130; 95 Daily Journal DAR 5409



April 25, 1995, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976 and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts III and IV.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Tuolumne County, No. 4075, William G. Polley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The case is remanded for a determination on the record of whether the battery is a felony or a misdemeanor. The court shall then impose the appropriate fines, making the appropriate findings. In all other respects, the judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Tuolumne County (California), which found that appellant drove without a valid driver's license and committed a battery.


OVERVIEW: The court found that appellant juvenile drove without a valid driver's license and committed a battery, and appellant sought review. The court remanded the case to the trial court to state whether the battery offense was a felony or a misdemeanor, and to consider appellant's ability to pay a restitution fine. The court affirmed the other aspects of the case, as appellant was not competent to waive his right to counsel where he had no rational comprehension of the charges and the proceedings, and was unable to properly realize the probable risks and consequences of his actions. The court found that the rule of convenience applied to a violation of Cal. Veh. Code § 12500, so the burden shifted to appellant to prove that he had a valid license. Appellant failed to produce any evidence that he possessed a valid driver's license.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court, which found that appellant juvenile drove without a valid driver's license and committed a battery, was affirmed, as appellant was not competent to waive his right to counsel and the rule of convenience applied to require appellant to prove that he had a valid driver's license. The cause was remanded to determine if the battery was a misdemeanor or felony.

 

806 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Gallo v. Acuna


No. H011802.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


48 Cal. App. 4th 641; 40 Cal. Rptr. 2d 589; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 385; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3050; 95 Daily Journal DAR 5205



April 24, 1995, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted July 27, 1995 (S046980), Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 4754.
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court. (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cites 34 Cal. App. 4th 136 and 39 Cal. App. 4th 184 and 43 Cal. App. 4th 1341.)]


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Santa Clara County, No. 729322, Robert Michael Foley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order authorizing the preliminary injunction is modified consistent with the views discussed herein; as modified, it is affirmed. Each party to bear its own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant alleged gang members appealed the order from the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), which granted respondent city's injunction, based on public nuisance law, to abate gang activity in a four-block neighborhood.


OVERVIEW: Appellant alleged gang members challenged the injunction to abate gang activity in a neighborhood and argued that it was unauthorized under the California Street Terrorism Enforcement and Prevention Act (STEP Act), Cal. Penal Code § 186.20, and civil nuisance laws, that it was violative of their U.S. Const. amend. I rights to speech and association, and that it was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. The court modified the injunction, affirmed it as modified, and held that the STEP Act was inapplicable because respondent city's complaint was based only on public nuisance law. The court held that the public nuisance law applied to criminal activity that interfered with the residents' use and enjoyment of their homes and streets. The court held that the injunction's prohibition against using words or symbols that referred to the gang and wearing clothing that bore the gang name was an infringement on protected U.S. Const. amend. I rights. The court struck down sections of the injunction for vagueness and overbreadth and held that mere membership in a gang was not a crime and noncriminal associational conduct by the gang members could not be enjoined on that basis alone.


OUTCOME: The judgment was modified and affirmed as modified because, insofar as the injunction reached no further than the United States Constitution allowed, it was properly used to abate gang-related criminal activity as a public nuisance.

 

807 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



U.D. Registry, Inc. v. State of California


No. B077282, No. B077283.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


34 Cal. App. 4th 107; 40 Cal. Rptr. 2d 228; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 378; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3046; 95 Daily Journal DAR 5197



April 21, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied August 17, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 5075. Cert. Denied January 16, 1996, 64 U.S.L. Week 3484.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Nos. BC044054 and BC044662, Harvey A. Schneider, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant renter challenged the judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which was entered in favor of appellee credit reporting agencies and held Cal. Civ. Code § 1785.13(a)(3) unconstitutional because it prohibited truthful reporting of information contained in court files that was fully available to the public and that could be freely reported and copied.


OVERVIEW: Appellant renter challenged the judgment that found unconstitutional Cal. Civ. Code § 1785.13(a)(3), a statute that prohibited disclosure of an unlawful detainer regarding a prospective tenant by a credit reporting agency, and only that form of disclosure. The court affirmed the judgment and held that a state could not completely suppress the dissemination of truthful information about lawful activity. The court held that the information that appellee credit reporting agencies sold was not commercial speech under U.S. Const. amend. I because it did not propose a commercial transaction, and the selling of the information did not raise it to the level of commercial speech. The information was lawfully retained and was truthful. The information was in the custody of the state because it was available through the court's public records. Although the state had an interest in the availability of rental housing for those needing it, that interest did not justify a ban on publication by credit reporting agencies of lawfully obtained and truthful information contained in court records open to the perusal of anyone.


OUTCOME: The judgment that disclosure could not be prohibited was affirmed because the information on credit reports regarding a tenant's involvement in unlawful detainer actions was not commercial speech, the information was lawfully obtained by appellee credit reporting agencies, and the information was truthful.

 

808 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Board of Supervisors v. Superior Court


No. D022160.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


33 Cal. App. 4th 1724; 39 Cal. Rptr. 2d 906; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 352; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2757; 67 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1203; 95 Daily Journal DAR 4762



April 14, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Docket Number and Name of this Case have been Corrected by the Court.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, Nos. 404148 and 588349, Arthur W. Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The petition for writ of review is granted as to the petitioner board of supervisors and the contempt order is vacated as to the Board. The superior court is directed to issue an order that the fines paid to date be returned to the Board. This disposition shall not affect the order of contempt with regard to the nonpetitioner sheriff. The stay is vacated upon this opinion becoming final. (Cal. Rules of Court, rule 24(a).) Each party shall bear its own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner County Board of Supervisors sought a writ of review directing respondent judge and inmates as real parties in interest, to vacate the order from the Superior Court of San Diego County (California) that adjudged board members and county sheriff in contempt and imposed fines for willful disobedience of a consent decree arising out of a jail overcrowding lawsuit. The sheriff had not joined the board as petitioner.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found petitioner county board of supervisors and the county sheriff in contempt of a consent decree for willfully disobeying the court-ordered inmate population cap imposed after a jail overcrowding lawsuit. Petitioner board, without the sheriff, sought a writ of review against respondent judge and inmates as real parties at interest, to vacate the contempt order and assessed fines. The court found that petitioner's only clear duties regarding the county jail were to provide the sheriff with food, clothing, and bedding for prisoners under Cal. Penal Code § 4015 and to pay other expenses incurred in keeping prisoners under Cal. Gov't Code § 29062 - not to oversee daily operations. The court concluded the contempt ruling did not require petitioner to take specific funding action or to reopen a closed facility. The court held there was insubstantial evidence to find petitioner had the ability to comply with the consent decree beyond its mandated statutory duties. The court granted a writ of review and vacated the contempt order for petitioner only and directed issuance of an order for repayment of fines to petitioner.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of review for petitioner county board of supervisors only but not the county sheriff, vacated the contempt order, and directed respondent judge and inmates as real parties in interest to issue an order returning paid fines to the board. The court found that the board did not willfully disobey the consent order in carrying out its legislative function within statutory and case law limitations.

 

809 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Ferguson v. Workers' Comp. Appeals Bd.


No. A063246.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


33 Cal. App. 4th 1613; 39 Cal. Rptr. 2d 806; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 354; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2748; 60 Cal. Comp. Cases 275; 95 Daily Journal DAR 4748



April 13, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied July 13, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 4455.


PRIOR HISTORY: WCAB No. OAK 177919.



DISPOSITION: The board's opinion and decision after reconsideration dated August 24, 1993, is annulled. The matter is remanded to the board for further proceedings consistent with the views expressed herein.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged the reconsideration order of the Worker's Compensation Appeals Board (California), which denied appellant's request for a 50 percent increase in the total disability award under Cal. Lab. Code § 4553 because of appellee employer's serious and willful misconduct. Appellant claimed that the 50 percent increase in the total disability award was not punitive.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employee was injured while working for appellee employer. The injury resulted in the need for medical treatment and vocational rehabilitation. Appellant was paid temporary disability indemnity and awarded a permanent disability indemnity of 61 percent. Appellant also sought a 50 percent increase in her award under Cal. Lab. Code § 4553, alleging serious and willful misconduct by appellee. The Worker's Compensation Appeals Board (board) granted reconsideration, affirmed the administrative law judge's finding of serious and willful misconduct, but held that the 50 percent increase applied only to compensation indemnity and not to nonindemnity benefits. The court annulled and remanded, holding that the 50 percent increase was not punitive in cases of serious and willful misconduct, and was to be calculated on the entire award, provided the total benefits did not exceed the amount necessary to fully compensate appellant.


OUTCOME: The Worker's Compensation Appeals Board's (board) decision in favor of appellee employer was annulled and remanded to the board for further proceedings consistent with the holding that the 50 percent increase was to be calculated on the entire award, not just compensation indemnity, provided the total benefits did not exceed the amount necessary to fully compensate appellant employee.

 

810 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Interinsurance Exchange v. Narula


No. E012417, No. E013717.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


33 Cal. App. 4th 1140; 39 Cal. Rptr. 2d 752; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 320; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2460; 95 Daily Journal DAR 4244



April 4, 1995, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for partial publication. Portions deleted are noted by the insertion of the following symbol at the points of ommission [[]].


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Bernardino County, No. RCV62566, William P. Hyde, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff creditor sought review of a judgment by the Superior Court of San Bernardino County (California), which sustained defendant personal representative of the estate's demurrer in plaintiff's claim against the estate to recover losses incurred as a result of the estate's rejection of its claim.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff creditor filed suit against defendant personal representative of the estate, to recover losses incurred as a result of defendant's rejection of plaintiff's claim. The claim was based upon a judgment from an auto accident whereby the deceased was to make monthly payments to plaintiff. The trial court sustained defendant's demurrer because plaintiff failed to follow the procedures of the California Probate Code. On appeal, plaintiff challenged the constitutionality of the Probate Code to the extent that it pertained to the administration of creditor claims against the estate of a decedent. The court rejected this argument and found the Probate Code to be constitutional because it was amended to give creditors more latitude in filing late claims and because it provided for actual notice to be sent to all known creditors. The court affirmed the judgment and held that plaintiff failed to allege facts sufficient to show that it complied with the late-claim remedy statute, Cal. Probate Code § 9103, and was still denied due process. The court also found that defendant could not have known of plaintiff until it filed the claim against the estate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that sustained defendant personal representative of the estate's rejection of plaintiff creditor's claim against the estate to recover losses incurred as a result of the rejection of the claim. The court held that the California Probate Code was constitutional and that plaintiff failed to avail itself of the late-claim statute and thus could not maintain its action.

 

811 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



B. C. Cotton, Inc. v. Voss


No. C016667.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


33 Cal. App. 4th 929; 39 Cal. Rptr. 2d 484; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 296; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2339; 95 Daily Journal DAR 3991



March 29, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Sacramento County, No. CV373955, James Timothy Ford, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and remanded to the trial court with directions to issue a new judgment consistent with the views expressed in this opinion. The parties shall bear their own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff cotton breeders appealed an order of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which denied all but one of their claims seeking declaratory and injunctive relief and a writ of mandate, after defendants denied their applications to plant nonapproved colored cotton. Defendants cross-appealed the trial court's holding that Cal. Food & Agric. Code § 52856 was unenforceable by virtue of being unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff cotton breeders' applications to plant colored cotton for breeding and testing purposes were denied. They sought declaratory and other relief, asserting violations of due process, equal protection, and statutory intent, and contended that the statutory scheme exceeded the legislature's police power and amounted to an uncompensated taking. The trial court held Cal. Food & Agric. Code § 52856 unconstitutionally vague and unenforceable, otherwise denying relief. The court held that, as erroneously interpreted by defendant state officials, the statute was improperly applied. Plaintiffs need not make their varieties available to other producers in order to engage in research and development or to seek approval for their varieties. However, the court disagreed that § 52856 was unconstitutionally vague. Defendants' regulations requiring plaintiffs to obtain permission for research and development of nonapproved varieties were held void as usurping legislative authority. While plaintiffs were entitled to judicial relief to that extent, the court otherwise rejected their challenge to the statutory and regulatory scheme governing the San Joaquin Valley Quality Cotton District.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded, with directions to issue a new judgment. The court agreed with the trial court's conclusion that defendant state officials incorrectly denied plaintiff cotton breeders' applications, but based on an incorrect statutory interpretation, not because the statute was unconstitutionally vague. The court also held that defendants' program regulations usurped authority not conferred by the legislature, and were thus void.

 

812 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Allen


No. B075756.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


33 Cal. App. 4th 1149; 40 Cal. Rptr. 2d 7; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 317; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2458; 95 Daily Journal DAR 4215



March 29, 1995, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts IV 1. and IV 2. b., c., and d.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. TA021230, Gary E. Daigh, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The sentence imposed for three counts of violating section 646.9, subdivision (b) is vacated, the judgment of conviction is modified to reflect a conviction in counts three, six, and seven for section 646.9, subdivision (a), and the judgment is further modified by imposing the misdemeanor sentence for the three section 646.9, subdivision (a) counts, execution of which sentence is stayed pursuant to section 654. In all other respects the judgment of conviction is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), where appellant received sentencing and convictions for terrorist threats pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 422, stalking, first degree residential burglary, and assault likely to produce great bodily injury with a deadly weapon.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of a judgment that convicted appellant of two counts of terrorist threats, three counts of stalking, first degree residential burglary, and assault likely to produce great bodily injury with a deadly weapon. Appellant challenged the conviction on several grounds. The court only addressed the sufficiency of the evidence that supported appellant's conviction of terrorist threats pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 422. Appellant argued that the evidence was not sufficient in supporting his conviction for terrorist threats because there was no showing that the victim sustained fear as required by § 422. The court held that the victim's 15 minutes of fear of appellant who was armed and who had made threats to the victim and her daughter constituted a sustained fear for purposes of § 422. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court modified appellant's sentencing on issues not described by the court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that convicted appellant of terrorist threats, stalking, first degree residential burglary, and assault likely to produce great bodily injury with a deadly weapon because evidence that victim was in fear for 15 minutes was sufficient to show "sustained fear." The court modified appellant's sentencing.

 

813 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Ireland


No. H012609.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


33 Cal. App. 4th 680; 39 Cal. Rptr. 2d 870; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 288; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2325; 95 Daily Journal DAR 3955



March 28, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied June 28, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Municipal Court of the Santa Cruz County Judicial District, No. 41-10745, Thomas Kelly, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Municipal Court of the Santa Cruz County Judicial District (California), which convicted him of driving with .08 percent or more, by weight, of alcohol in his blood. Defendant, whose conviction was based on a breath test, contended that he was denied due process where he was not allowed to adduce evidence as to the variability between blood and breath-alcohol measurements.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped by an officer for speeding. The officer smelled alcohol coming from defendant's vehicle. Defendant was permitted to choose between a blood test and a breath test. He elected a breath test whose results showed an alcohol concentration of between 0.10 and 0.11 percent. Defendant was convicted under Cal. Veh. Code § 23152(b) (1990) of driving with .08 percent or more, by weight, of alcohol in his blood. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that the legislature's prohibition against driving with a certain amount of breath alcohol concentration was within its power to regulate driving. The court held that proscribing defendant from adducing evidence as to the variability of blood and breath alcohol measurements did not violate his right to due process. Section 23152(b) did not require breath alcohol to be converted to blood alcohol concentration, but rather provided that the breath alcohol ratio would apply when the breath test was used regardless of its blood alcohol conversion value. The statute did not presume intoxication but defined the substantive offense as driving with a specified concentration of alcohol.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant for driving with .08 percent or more, by weight, of alcohol in his blood. The court held that preventing defendant, whose conviction was based on a breath test, from adducing evidence as to the variability between blood and breath-alcohol measurements did not deny him due process where the statute provided that the breath alcohol ratio would apply when the breath test was used.

 

814 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Littoral Development Co. v. San Francisco Bay Conservation etc. Com.


No. A064842.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


33 Cal. App. 4th 211; 39 Cal. Rptr. 2d 266; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 249; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2034; 95 Daily Journal DAR 3451



March 17, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied June 15, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Marin County, No. 158041, Gary W. Thomas, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, land developers, challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Marin County (California), which denied appellants' petitions to have a portion of land declared as not marshland subject to the authority of respondent San Francisco Bay Conservation and Development Commission and to declare respondent's actions as an unlawful regulatory taking.


OVERVIEW: Respondent San Francisco Bay Conservation and Development Commission filed an action to have appellant land developers vacate land respondent wanted declared marshland and subject to their jurisdiction. The trial court granted a stay pending the decision in another case, which would resolve the jurisdictional dispute. Respondent appealed the stay, but during the pendency of the appeal, the collateral case was adjudicated with a finding that only a portion of the property was marshland. Respondent dismissed its appeal, but the court nonetheless addressed appellants' issues regarding the denial of a declaratory judgment. The court held that the claim that a portion of appellants' property was marshland was barred by collateral estoppel and res judicata, and that, even if it were not so barred, the claim still would have no basis. The court held that respondent's actions did not constitute an unconstitutional taking because no portion of the property had been taken and there was no taking merely because of the time spent to adjudicate the jurisdictional issues. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, holding that appellant land developer's claim that a portion of the land was not marshland was barred by res judicata and collateral estoppel and appellant's claim of unconstitutional regulatory taking was moot because respondent San Francisco Bay Conservation and Development Commission was no longer claiming jurisdiction over the nonmarshland portion of appellants' property.

 

815 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Wilder


Nos. D020002, D021351, No. D021351.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


33 Cal. App. 4th 90; 39 Cal. Rptr. 2d 247; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 237; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1972; 95 Daily Journal DAR 3333



March 15, 1995, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. 1 


1 Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts IV.-VII.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied June 14, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, No. CR87535, Elizabeth N. Kutzner, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order is affirmed. The petition for a writ of habeas corpus is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which ruled in favor of respondent district attorney and extended appellant's commitment to the department of mental health for an additional two years under Cal. Penal Code § 1026.5.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found appellant not guilty of residential burglary by reason of insanity and appellant was committed to the department of mental health. Respondent district attorney petitioned under Cal. Penal Code § 1026.5 to extend appellant's commitment for an additional two years. The trial court extended the commitment. Appellant sought review of the trial court's decision. The court affirmed the trial court and denied appellant's petition. The court held that § 1026.5 was constitutional because due process did not require that the standard for legal insanity under the M'Naghten test and the standard for extension of commitment for an insanity acquittee be identical. The extended commitment had a reasonable relation to the purpose of commitment. A jury instruction on the meaning of mental disease, defect, or disorder was not required because its meaning was explained in the testimony. Appellant was not denied equal protection because there was a rational basis for the different treatment of insanity acquittees and civilly committed individuals. An insanity acquittee placed mental health at issue and demonstrated dangerousness by committing a criminal offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that ruled in favor of respondent district attorney and extended appellant's commitment to the department of mental health for an additional two years because due process did not require the standard for the extension of a commitment for an insanity acquittee to be identical to the legal insanity standard, and appellant was not denied equal protection because there was a rational basis.

Burchett v. City of Newport Beach


No. G014383.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


33 Cal. App. 4th 1472; 40 Cal. Rptr. 2d 1; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 337; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2647; 95 Daily Journal DAR 4511



March 10, 1995, Decided


NOTICE:   [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published April 10, 1995.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied May 25, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 3559.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Orange County, No. 687091, Randell L. Wilkinson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants property owners sought review of judgment of the Superior Court of Orange County (California), which dismissed their complaint seeking damages from respondents, city and city officials, and granted motions to quash service on respondents, city and retired manager, pursuant to Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 415.20(b), after respondents, public works department and council, refused to grant an encroachment permit for appellants' front driveway.


OVERVIEW: Appellants property owners' application for an encroachment permit to use the front driveway to their property was denied by respondents, public works department and council. Appellants filed a complaint for damages against respondents, city and city officials, and asserted breach of agreement, breach of fiduciary duty, fraud, bad faith, denial of equal protection and due process, and deprivation of civil rights. Respondents, city and retired city manager, received service of appellants' complaint by substituted service and filed a motion to quash the service. Respondents, city and its manager, filed a demurrer which was sustained without leave to amend and the complaint was dismissed. On appeal, the court affirmed the order of the trial court which dismissed the complaint and held that service on respondents city and retired city manager was properly quashed pursuant to Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 415.20(b), because of appellants' failed to properly serve them. The court found no error in the trial court's order which sustained the demurrer because appellants failed to show how their complaint would be amended to state a cause of action and to file an opposition.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment which dismissed appellants property owners' complaint and found no error in order which quashed service on respondents, city and retired city manager, because appellants failed to properly serve them. The court held that respondents' demurrer was properly sustained because appellants failed to show how complaint would be amended to state cause of action and file an opposition to demurrer.

 

817 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


Anderson v. Superior Court


No. F022848.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


36 Cal. App. 4th 1537; 38 Cal. Rptr. 2d 890; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 222; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1892; 95 Daily Journal DAR 3208



March 9, 1995, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted June 1, 1995 (S046006), Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 3719.
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court. (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cite 32 Cal. App. 4th 1716.)] (See 11 Cal. 4th 1152)


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding for Writ of Mandate by Susan B.



DISPOSITION: Let a writ of mandate issue commanding the superior court to vacate Rule 22, and to allow petitioner reasonable attorneys fees.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner county clerk sought a writ of mandate to compel respondent, the Superior Court of Fresno County (California), to vacate a local rule, adopted under the authority of Cal. Gov't Code § 69898, which appointed the superior court executive officer to serve as the clerk of the superior court and removed that office from petitioner.


OVERVIEW: Respondent, the Superior Court of Fresno County, adopted a local rule under the authority of Cal. Gov't Code § 69898, which appointed the superior court executive officer to serve as the clerk of the superior court and removed that office from petitioner county clerk. Petitioner sought a writ of mandate to declare respondents' adoption of the rule to be an abuse of discretion. The court let the writ issue and held that respondent did not have the authority under § 69898 to accomplish the transfer by rule of court. The voters chose petitioner to carry out clerk duties. The voters thus had a constitutional right to have those duties carried out by petitioner. Because the California legislature is subject to the California constitution, it would not have had the power to transfer clerk duties from petitioner to the superior court executive officer during petitioner's term. Since the legislature could not delegate a power it did not itself have, it could not give such a power to respondent through the enactment of a statute. The inherent power of courts to conduct their business is subject to constitutional limitations.


OUTCOME: The court let a writ of mandate issue that commanded respondent, the Superior Court of Fresno County, to vacate its rule because the inherent power of the courts to conduct their assigned business was subject to the constitutional right of voters to have the duties of elected officials carried out by petitioner county clerk.

Feminist Women's Health Center v. Blythe


No. C011874.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


32 Cal. App. 4th 1641; 39 Cal. Rptr. 2d 189; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 218; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1837



March 8, 1995, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. *


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts I and II.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied June 1, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sacramento County, No. 506341, James L. Long, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The attorney fee order is reversed as to defendants Walker and Operation Rescue. In all other respects, the judgment and attorney fee order are affirmed. Defendants Blythe, Lewis, Reali, Baggett and Stoos shall pay plaintiff's costs on appeal. Plaintiff shall pay the costs on appeal of defendants Walker and Operation Rescue.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant antiabortion demonstrators and respondent health clinic submitted briefs at the invitation of the Court of Appeal of California, Third Appellate District, for the court to reconsider its prior decision affirming the trial court's permanent injunction imposing time, place, and manner restrictions on appellants' demonstrations at respondent's location.


OVERVIEW: Appellant antiabortion demonstrators challenged a permanent injunction issued by the trial court, which imposed time, manner, and place restrictions on appellants' demonstrations in front of respondent health clinic. The court of appeals originally affirmed the trial court's judgment, then, following instructions from the United States Supreme Court in a related case, invited the parties to submit briefs so it could reconsider. The court affirmed the injunction again, holding that the injunction's restrictions on appellants' free speech were content-neutral, and were reasonable because appellants' actions threatened a significant level of harm to respondent's patients, even though appellants had not offered violence. The court held that appellants' actions unreasonably interfered with respondent's patients' constitutional right to privacy, which was afforded a greater level of protection under Cal. Const. art. I, § 1, than under U.S. Const. amend. I. The court reversed the award of attorney's fees against two appellants, because a default judgment had been issued against them and the attorney's fees award violated Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 580.


OUTCOME: The court republished its prior decision, affirmed the permanent injunction imposing restrictions on appellant antiabortion demonstrators, because appellants' actions, although not threatening violence, did threaten a significant level of harm to respondent's patients. The court reversed the award of attorney's fees for respondent health clinic as to two appellants only, because a default judgment had been entered against them.

Board of Supervisors v. Superior Court


No. B085744.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


32 Cal. App. 4th 1616; 38 Cal. Rptr. 2d 876; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 211; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1800



March 7, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified March 9, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. BC095705, Donald E. Smallwood, Temporary Judge. * 


* Pursuant to California Constitution, article VI, section 21.



DISPOSITION: The alternative writ is discharged. The petition is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Los Angeles County Board of Supervisors filed a petition for writ of mandate or prohibition and a request for stay in the Court of Appeal of California, Second Appellate District, Division Three, challenging respondent trial court's determination that plaintiff judges' association could conduct discovery of extrinsic evidence on the question of whether petitioner complied with Cal. Gov't Code § 26639(b).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff judges' association challenged the decision of petitioner Los Angeles County Board of Supervisors to consolidate court-related services to the county sheriff's office. Respondent trial court ruled that plaintiff could conduct discovery of extrinsic evidence concerning whether petitioner's members took the judges' vote into advisement, as required by Cal. Gov't Code § 26639(b). Petitioner filed a request for writ of mandamus to prohibit the discovery. The court granted the writ, reversing the trial court's decision and holding that to permit plaintiff to conduct discovery into the mental processes of petitioner's members would constitute judicial inquiry into motives behind legislation, which would violate the separation of powers doctrines of the U.S. Constitution and Cal. Const. art. III, § 3.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of mandamus against respondent trial court, because to permit plaintiff judges' association to conduct discovery into extrinsic evidence regarding the mental processes of petitioner Los Angeles County Board of Supervisors in its determination to consolidate court functions to the sheriff's office would violate the doctrine of separation of powers.

 

820 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. $31,500 in United States Currency


No. C017650.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


32 Cal. App. 4th 1442; 38 Cal. Rptr. 2d 836; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 197; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1691



March 3, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing March 29, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 315.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Joaquin County, No. 257683, K. Peter Saiers, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed. The parties shall bear their own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of the decision from the Superior Court of San Joaquin County (California) that, in a civil asset forfeiture proceeding for forfeiture of property connected with drug trafficking, entered summary judgment and judgment on the pleadings in favor of respondent claimants.


OVERVIEW: Police stopped respondent claimants' car. Since neither respondent had a driver's license, police had the car towed. An inventory of the car disclosed four ounces of marijuana, $ 31,500 cash, and a cellular phone. One respondent was issued a citation for possession of marijuana and released. Respondents were served with notice of nonjudicial forfeiture proceedings for the cash and cellular phone. Appellant, the state, challenged the summary judgment and judgment on the pleadings entered in favor of respondents. Appellant argued the trial court erred in determining a criminal conviction for drug trafficking was a prerequisite to forfeiture. The court found that the statutes, 1988 Cal. Stat. 1492, were in effect at the time of the seizure of property and at the time the action was filed in the trial court. The effect of the 1994 law, 1994 Cal. Stat. 314, was to continue in force the same law that applied when the case arose. At all times since seizure of the contested property there was an asset forfeiture law in California, which did not require a criminal conviction as a prerequisite to forfeiture of the property at issue in this case. The judgment was reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that, in a civil asset forfeiture proceeding for forfeiture of property connected with drug trafficking, entered summary judgment and judgment on the pleadings in favor of respondents because California's asset forfeiture law did not require a criminal conviction as a prerequisite to forfeiture of the property.

People v. Hernandez


No. B078800.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


32 Cal. App. 4th 1248; 38 Cal. Rptr. 2d 605; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 196; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1639



March 2, 1995, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied June 1, 1995 and the Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 3735.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. VA019047, C. Robert Simpson, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), after he pleaded no contest to discharging a firearm with gross negligence, under Cal. Penal Code § 246.3, and was sentenced to probation with drug-related conditions, on the ground that the conditions of probation were unreasonable and unconstitutional and that his due process rights were violated because he was not allowed to speak at sentencing.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with, inter alia, discharging a firearm with gross negligence, under Cal. Penal Code § 246.3, after sheriff's deputies observed him shoot a handgun into the air while riding in the bed of a pickup truck. The probation report recommended drug-related conditions of probation because of a history of drug use. Prior to sentencing, the superior court asked appellant if he had any legal cause; appellant answered, "no." Appellant was sentenced to probation with drug-related conditions. Appellant asked to address the court and was denied. Appellant argued that the drug-related conditions of his probation were unconstitutional and that his due process rights were violated when he was not permitted to speak at sentencing. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that the drug-related conditions of probation were not unconstitutional, as they were reasonably related to appellant's rehabilitation, given his history of drug use, and they were not overdrawn, and that there was no prejudicial error in the trial court's refusal to let appellant speak at sentencing, as the superior court complied with Cal. Penal Code § 1200 and appellant was represented by counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, holding that the drug-related conditions of appellant's probation for discharging a firearm with gross negligence were not unconstitutional, as they were reasonably related to appellant's rehabilitation, given his history of drug use, and were not overdrawn, and that there was no prejudicial error in the trial court's refusal to let appellant speak at sentencing, as appellant was represented by counsel.

 

822 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


Los Angeles County Dep't of Children's Servs. (In re Sade C.)


No. B082230, No. B084043.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


32 Cal. App. 4th 1225; 38 Cal. Rptr. 2d 822; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 199; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1632



March 2, 1995, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Granted March 16, 1995. Rehearing Opinion of August 11, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 793. (See 37 Cal. App. 4th 88)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Nos. LK00851 and CK09428, Larry P. Fidler, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The appeal from the judgment terminating the parental rights of Gregory C. is dismissed. The appeal from the order declaring Vanessa R. a dependent child of the juvenile court is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, indigent parents, sought review of the decisions from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) that, in one case, terminated their parental rights, and in another case declared a child a dependent child of the juvenile court, pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code §§ 300, 366.26.


OVERVIEW: The court consolidated two unrelated appeals where appellants, indigent parents, had Wende briefs filed, to address the issue of mandatory independent judicial review of dependency cases: (1) termination of parental rights and (2) dependency adjudication. The court found that there was no previously established constitutional right to counsel in proceedings affecting parental rights. The automatic right to counsel afforded in California proceedings affecting parental rights was only statutory. There was no right to a Wende review in dependency proceedings. The delay necessary to perform a Wende review was tolerable only if there was a substantial likelihood that Wende reviews would avoid a serious risk of parental rights being erroneously restricted or terminated. Such a risk did not exist in dependency cases. The court concluded that on appeal from orders under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code §§ 300, 366.26 adjudicating dependency and terminating parental rights, where counsel for an appellant filed a brief raising no issues, the reviewing court was not required to conduct its own independent review of the record. The appeals were dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeals because, from orders adjudicating dependency and terminating parental rights, the reviewing court was not required to conduct its own independent review of the record where counsel for an indigent appellant filed a Wende brief raising no issues.

People v. Stanfield


No. B082070.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


32 Cal. App. 4th 1152; 38 Cal. Rptr. 2d 328; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 168; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1536; 95 Daily Journal DAR 2613



February 28, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied June 1, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. GA016562, J. Michael Byrne, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment rendered by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) that convicted her for making terrorist threats.


OVERVIEW: Appellant threatened that if her former attorney did not join her in bringing her Universe Reform Party into power, she would hire gang members to kill him. Defendant was convicted for making terrorist threats and sought review of the judgment. Appellate decisions were in conflict as to whether the conditional language used in the threat by appellant supported a conviction under Cal. Penal Code § 422. The court concluded that conditionality was only one circumstance to be considered in the overall analysis of whether the threat was a true threat, and it was not a bright line separating actionable threats from protected ones. Appellant's substantial evidence challenge was not met with favor by the reviewing court. The court affirmed appellant's conviction. The court found that appellant's threat contained a considerable degree of unconditionality since compliance with defendant's condition would be practically impossible. Further, the other three factors in § 422 were also met because appellant's threats and conduct aimed at her former attorney was, in significant degrees unequivocal, immediate, and specific.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for making terrorist threats because there was substantial evidence to show that her threat contained a considerable degree of unconditionality and was unequivocal and immediate.

People v. Peneda


No. G014338.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


32 Cal. App. 4th 1022; 38 Cal. Rptr. 2d 312; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 175; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1557; 95 Daily Journal DAR 2658



February 27, 1995, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. *


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts II and IV.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Orange County, No. C-94527, Jean M. Rheinheimer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from the Superior Court of Orange County (California), in which he was convicted for conspiracy to transport cocaine and the transportation and possession of that cocaine for sale. The jury found the total amount of cocaine exceeded 100 pounds in weight which enhanced defendant's sentence by 15 years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for conspiracy to transport cocaine and the transportation and possession of that cocaine for sale. The jury determined the total amount of cocaine exceeded 100 pounds in weight which enhanced defendant's sentence by 15 years. An expert testified at defendant's trial that 100 pounds of cocaine was actually contained within the white powder seized by the police and arrived at the conclusion based on a probability calculation of samples taken from the whole amount. The expert received bricks of cocaine seized from defendant's homes and tested several bricks which he weighed and analyzed and each tested positive for cocaine. Defendant objected to this evidence. The court affirmed the conviction holding that the probability calculations used were a long established scientific method for testing theories and the use of extrapolations based on randomly selected samples is accepted in the scientific community.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction for conspiracy to transport cocaine and the transportation and possession of that cocaine for sale because the probability calculation methods used by the expert were long established scientific methods for testing theories and accepted in the scientific community.

In re Jacqueline L.


No. G015316.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


33 Cal. App. 4th 325; 39 Cal. Rptr. 2d 178; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 266; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2193; 95 Daily Journal DAR 3730



February 21, 1995, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published March 22, 1995. Review Denied May 11, 1995 and the Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI; § 14; rule 976 Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 3351.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Orange County, Nos. J422305 and J423264, Robert H. Keefe, Temporary Judge. * 


* Pursuant to California Constitution, article VI, section 21.



DISPOSITION: The order of the juvenile court selecting guardianship instead of adoption and ordering four weeks of visitation each summer with the father's relatives and Kiowa and Comanche Tribes is reversed. The case is remanded to the juvenile court with directions to enter a new order placing the children for adoption and terminating the rights of the parents.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Orange County Social Service Agency appealed the order of the Superior Court of Orange County (California) refusing, after considering Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 366.26 and the Indian Child Welfare Act, 25 U.S.C.S. § 1901 et seq., foster parents permission to adopt two Indian children abandoned by their parents, but ordering a guardianship with required visitation to defendant father's Oklahoma tribe as the best permanent plan.


OVERVIEW: After parents abandoned two Indian children, and reunification plans failed, the trial court decided, under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 366.26, that rather than let the foster parents adopt them, they would be under a guardianship with a required annual four-week stay with the defendant father's Oklahoma tribe. Plaintiff Orange County Social Service Agency appealed. Reversing the decision, the court ruled that when children could not have been returned to their parents, and were likely to be adopted, any selection other than adoption must have been sufficiently weighty to offset a child's need for a stable, permanent home. The court found the increased cultural benefits from forming a bond with the father's tribe did not outweigh legislatively preferred adoption, adding that the trial court found that any removal from the foster parents would cause irreparable emotional damage. The court held that the Indian Child Welfare Act, 25 U.S.C.S § 1901 et seq., was not violated because the affected tribes were given the opportunity to intervene early in the proceeding, and the case was not one of children living on a reservation being snatched from a tribe by overzealous social workers.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision, appealed by plaintiff Orange County Social Services Agency, in a case in which defendant father's tribe participated, deciding on a guardianship for two Indian children abandoned by their parents. The court remanded the matter to the court with directions to enter an order placing the children for adoption and terminating parental rights.

 

826 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



City of San Jose v. Superior Court


No. H013078.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


32 Cal. App. 4th 330; 38 Cal. Rptr. 2d 205; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 127; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1180; 95 Daily Journal DAR 2046



February 15, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied May 25, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 3564.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Santa Clara County, No. 736204, Socrates Peter Manoukian, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner city sought expedited review of a writ of mandate issued by the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California) in favor of real parties in interest protesters, that declared a city ordinance outlawing targeted picketing within 300 feet of a targeted residence unconstitutional under U.S. Const. amend. I.


OVERVIEW: Protesters were charged with anti-abortion picketing within the proscribed distance of the homes of staff members of an abortion clinic, a misdemeanor violation of the City of San Jose Municipal Code. On petition for extraordinary review, the superior court issued a writ of mandate directing the municipal court to sustain protesters' demurrers that were granted in municipal court. Although the superior court determined that the ordinance was content neutral and not vague, and that it left open, ample, and alternative channels of communication, it was under compulsion of a decision of the United States Supreme Court that ruled a 300-foot buffer zone was unconstitutionally broad. The court reversed the superior court's ruling, finding that the ordinance was a less onerous, bright line standard intended to protect an important privacy interest, that of residential privacy, which includes protection of the unwilling listener in his home, and that protesters failed to show that the ordinance was substantially broader than necessary to protect the right of residential privacy involved, and that as a matter of law they had no alternative channels of communication.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's grant of the writ of prohibition, stating that respondent superior court and real parties in interest protesters could not demonstrate that the conclusions justifying the ordinance were so unreasonable and arbitrary as to be beyond the power of the legislature, and commanded respondent to vacate its order and to issue a new order denying the petition for writ of prohibition.
