People v. King


No. A060701.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


43 Cal. App. 4th 1770; 36 Cal. Rptr. 2d 365; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 1182; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8882; 94 Daily Journal DAR 16461



November 22, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted March 2, 1995 (S044061), Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 1558.
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cites 30 Cal. App. 4th 328 and 34 Cal. App. 4th 1576 and 39 Cal. App. 4th 744.)] On June 26, 1996, review dismissed and cause remanded to Court of Appeal, First Appellate District, Division Three, Reported at: 1996 Cal. LEXIS 3603.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Contra Costa County, No. 922276-1, Wayne A. Westover, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgments against King, Joseph, and Canada are modified to reflect a stay, pursuant to Penal Code section 654, of their sentences on count two, violation of Penal Code section 591. As modified, the judgments are affirmed. The judgment against Dickerson is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Contra Costa County (California), in which a jury convicted them of robbery in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 211 and destruction of telephone lines in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 591.


OVERVIEW: After receiving a dispatch regarding an armed robbery at a motel, officers observed a vehicle driving away from the motel, and stopped the vehicle after discovering the registration was expired, informed defendant why she was stopped, and that they were investigating a robbery. Officers discovered other individuals in the vehicle, matching the descriptions from the dispatch and arrested them. Defendants were convicted of robbery and destruction of phone lines, pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 211 and § 591, respectively. Defendants appealed contending the trial court erred in denying their motions to suppress evidence because the stop was an illegal pretext to search the vehicle and contended that Cal. Penal Code § 654 compelled a stay of their sentences for destruction of phone lines. The court affirmed the convictions and held the stop was proper and not pretextual in nature. The court reasoned that under the objective test, the officers did not exceed the scope of their authority hence, defendants' detention was legally authorized. Further, the court modified the sentences regarding the destruction offenses because the offense was part of the indivisible transaction of the robbery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgments convicting defendants of robbery and modified their sentences regarding the destruction of phone lines. The court held the trial court properly denied defendants' motions to suppress evidence from the search because the stop was not pretextual, thus the search was validly authorized. Further, because the destruction offense arose out of the robbery offense, defendants' sentences were stayed.

Hansen Brothers Enterprises v. Board of Supervisors


No. C017070.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


39 Cal. App. 4th 727; 35 Cal. Rptr. 2d 358; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 1152; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8723; 94 Daily Journal DAR 16118



November 15, 1994, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted February 16, 1995 (S044011), Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 859.
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cites 30 Cal. App. 4th 23 and 34 Cal. App. 4th 1546.)] (See 12 Cal. 4th 533)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Nevada County, No. 41465, Reginald Littrell, Judge. * 


* Judge of the Sierra Superior Court sitting under assignment by the Chairperson of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mining company sought review of a decision of the Superior Court, Nevada County (California) that denied appellant's petition for a writ of administrative mandate to compel respondents, the county board of supervisors, to approve a reclamation plan based on substantial future increases in mining activities.


OVERVIEW: In response to the Surface Mining and Reclamation Act, Cal Pub. Res. Code § 2710 et seq., appellant mining company asked respondents, the county board of supervisors, to approve a plan based on substantial future increases in mining activities on appellant's property. When the county declined, appellant petitioned for a writ of administrative mandate to require the county to approve the plan. The trial court denied the petition and appellant sought review. The court noted that while enactment of zoning ordinances was a legitimate use of the police power, if a zoning ordinance impaired the vested right in an existing use of property, the owner's due process right to continued use of the property could overcome the police power. However, the court held that appellant's reclamation plan went far beyond the existing use because it proposed a large increase in the current level of mining on the property. The court affirmed, holding that intensification of a previous use, even if intended by the property owner at the time the zoning ordinance was passed, was not part of appellant's vested rights and did not take precedence over respondent's zoning plan.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment declining appellant mining company's petition for a writ of administrative mandate because it held that the proposed intensification of mining activities on appellant's land was not part of appellant's vested rights and did not take precedence over respondent's zoning plan.

People v. Strong


No. E013024.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


30 Cal. App. 4th 366; 35 Cal. Rptr. 2d 494; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 1174; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8847; 94 Daily Journal DAR 16343



November 15, 1994, Decided  
November 15, 1994


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. ** 


** Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts II, III, and IV.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Riverside County, No. CR-47822, William R. Bailey, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant prisoner sought review of his convictions from the Superior Court of Riverside County (California) for the unlawful taking or driving a vehicle and for receiving stolen property.


OVERVIEW: Defendant prisoner contended that he was improperly convicted both of unlawful taking under Cal. Veh. Code § 10851 and receiving stolen property under Cal. Penal Code § 496 as to the same stolen vehicle. The court noted that generally the thief could not have been convicted of both the theft and of receiving stolen property. However, a recent change to Cal. Penal Code § 496, meant that the fact that the jury may have found that defendant unlawfully took the pickup no longer barred his conviction for receiving or withholding the pickup. The court stated that if the evidence showed only one continuous violation of Cal. Veh. Code § 10851, in which the driving was part and parcel of the taking, then a conviction for driving or taking under Cal. Veh. Code § 10851 was a conviction for theft of the same property which barred conviction under Cal. Penal Code § 496. The court stated that the car was stolen four days before defendant was found driving it. The court held that no reasonable juror could have found that at the time defendant was found driving the vehicle he was still engaged in the original taking; thus, the trial court's order was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Defendant prisoner's convictions for driving a stolen vehicle and theft of a vehicle were affirmed because the theft of the vehicle and the driving of the stolen vehicle were two independent crimes.

People v. Ruge


No. B073525


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR.


29 Cal. App. 4th 1811; 35 Cal. Rptr. 2d 830; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 1150; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8700; 94 Daily Journal DAR 16077



November 14, 1994, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied February 23, 1995 and the Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct., Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 1107.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, BA042011, Carol J. Fieldhouse, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgments as to both appellants Ruge and Restrepo on count 1, possession for sale and the respective weight enhancements, are reversed. We also reverse the finding as to counts 4 and 5 relating to the 25-pound weight enhancement and the 10-pound weight enhancement as to count 6.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) that upheld a jury verdict that found appellants guilty of various counts of cocaine possession, conspiracy, and transportation charges.


OVERVIEW: Narcotics agents conducted extensive surveillance of appellants, two males. The agents' surveillance culminated in two seizures of large amounts of cocaine. Appellants were charged with various counts of cocaine possession, conspiracy, and transportation charges. At trial, during deliberations, the jury submitted an inquiry as to reasonable doubt, possession, and other issues. The trial judge deviated from the standard instructions, using various illustrations. The trial judge also refused to answer the jury's question relating to deadlock. The jury found appellants guilty on all counts. The court reversed as to the possession charge, but otherwise affirmed. The court held that although clarification was authorized, diverging from the standard reasonable doubt instruction was not advised. The trial court's error in instructing the jury was not harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court reversed as to the possession charge, but otherwise affirmed. The court held that the trial court's error in instructing the jury was not harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. Although clarification was authorized, diverging from the standard reasonable doubt instruction was not advised.

Lackner v. Department of Health Services


No. A063069.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE.


29 Cal. App. 4th 1760; 35 Cal. Rptr. 2d 482; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 1137; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8604; 94 Daily Journal DAR 15917



November 10, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied January 25, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 398.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, No. 949902, Stuart R. Pollak, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), in which the trial court had found Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § l40l6.5 to be constitutional, the statute provided that Medi-Cal beneficiaries would be assigned to and enrolled in a managed care plan unless the Medi-Cal beneficiary timely elected to obtain services from a fee-for-service provider.


OVERVIEW: Appellant citizens, plaintiffs below, challenged the constitutionality of Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § l40l6.5, which provided that Medi-Cal beneficiaries would be assigned to and enrolled in a managed care plan unless the Medi-Cal beneficiary timely elected to obtain services from a fee-for-service provider. Appellants had filed a petition for writ of mandamus seeking to restrain implementation of § 14016.5 as an illegal expenditure of public funds, alleging that § 14016.5 violated the due process clauses of the federal and state constitutions and violated the right of privacy guaranteed by the state constitution. Appellants contended that this "default" provision forced certain Medi-Cal recipients to be involuntarily enrolled in a managed care plan and denied them their right to choose their own health care provider. The court affirmed, holding that actionable invasions of privacy must have been sufficiently serious in their nature, scope, and actual or potential impact to constitute an egregious breach of the social norms underlying the privacy right. Absent an infringement upon a constitutional right, the statute was upheld where it met the rational basis test.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, holding that the statute, which provided that Medi-Cal beneficiaries would be assigned to and enrolled in a managed care plan unless the Medi-Cal beneficiary timely elected to obtain services from a fee-for-service provider, was not so seriously serious in nature, scope, and actual or potential impact so as to infringe upon a constitutional right. The statute had also met the rational basis test.

City of South Pasadena v. Department of Transportation


No. C017135.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


29 Cal. App. 4th 1280; 35 Cal. Rptr. 2d 113; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 1099; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8281; 94 Daily Journal DAR 15923



October 28, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing November 22, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 1183.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sacramento County, No. CV533468, Earl Warren, Jr., Judge. * 


* Retired judge of the Sacramento Municipal Court sitting under assignment by the Chairperson of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: Caltrans's motion to dismiss the appeal and cross-appeal as moot is denied. The judgment is affirmed. The parties shall bear their own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Both defendant, Department of Transportation, and plaintiff city sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which declared that, under Cal. Sts. & High. Code § 100.4, time for defendant to select a route for a new freeway had run, and further enjoined defendant from constructing a freeway through the city without an agreement pursuant to Cal. Sts. & High. Code § 100.2.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, Department of Transportation, was responsible for selecting the route for a new freeway. Plaintiff city requested the trial court to declare that the time for selecting a route had expired under Cal. Sts. & High. Code § 100.4 . The trial court held that time had run and enjoined defendant from building a freeway through the city without a freeway agreement pursuant to Cal. Sts. & High. Code § 100.2. Both parties appealed. Defendant claimed that a proposed amendment to § 100.4 would eliminate the debated time limitations and that, therefore, the appeal and cross-appeal was moot. The court affirmed, holding that until the amendment took effect, the time limitations were still in place. Plaintiff argued that the court should broaden the injunction by enforcing against defendant its own policy of obtaining freeway agreements even when not strictly required by § 100.2, that is, when no street would be permanently closed. This assertion was without merit because there was no proposal to build a freeway through the city that did not permanently close any street. The court therefore upheld the injunction as issued.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision enjoining defendant, Department of Transportation, from further planning, route approval, and construction of a new freeway because the statutorily prescribed time for selecting a route for the freeway had expired.

People v. Wiener


No. D019745.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


29 Cal. App. 4th 1300; 35 Cal. Rptr. 2d 321; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 1107; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8291; 94 Daily Journal DAR 15309



October 28, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied January 25, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 412.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, No. FF151308, Norbert Ehrenfreund, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order denying the motion to reinstate the first two causes of action is reversed. The superior court is directed to grant the motion and return the matter to the municipal court for further proceedings consistent with the views expressed in this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which denied plaintiff's motion to reinstate those portions of the complaint charging defendants with conspiracy to distribute obscene matter in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 311.2.


OVERVIEW: The municipal court found a provision of California's obscene matter statutes, Cal. Penal Code §§ 311.2, invalid as applied to distributors of such matter under the right to privacy set forth in Cal. Const. art. I, § 1 and struck two counts of the complaint against defendants. The state appealed an order of the superior court denying their motion to reinstate those portions of the complaint. Defendants claimed that as distributors of obscene matter, they had standing to assert their customers' privacy right to possess and acquire obscene matter. The court reversed, holding that defendants did not have a legally protected privacy interest under Cal. Const. art. I, § 1. Unable to rely on a derivative privacy interest, defendants also could not establish a reasonable expectation of privacy. The superior court erred in denying the motion to reinstate the causes of action. The superior court was directed to grant the motion and return the matter to the municipal court for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order denying the state's motion to reinstate two causes of action charging defendants with conspiracy to distribute obscene matter and with violating Cal. Penal Code § 311.2 because defendants were unable to rely on a derivative privacy interest, based on its customers' right to posses and acquire obscene matter, to establish a reasonable expectation of privacy.

Brosterhous v. State Bar


No. C015318.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


39 Cal. App. 4th 417; 35 Cal. Rptr. 2d 86; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 1093; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8228; 94 Daily Journal DAR 15194



October 27, 1994, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted February 23, 1995 (S043692), Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 1091.
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court. (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cites 29 Cal. App. 4th 963 and 34 Cal. App. 4th 810.)] (See 12 Cal. 4th 315)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sacramento County, No. CV527974, Ronald B. Robie, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and the matter remanded to the trial court with directions to vacate its order sustaining defendants' demurrer and to enter an order overruling it. Plaintiffs are to recover their costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, members of state bar, appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California) that sustained defendant state bar's general demurrer without leave to amend and dismissed plaintiffs' action, which claimed a violation of their rights under U.S. Const. amend. I.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, members of state bar, objected to defendant state bar's determination of the amount of each member's dues that were attributable to defendant's non-chargeable activities, and thus, were permitted to have been subtracted from each member's dues payment. Plaintiffs contended that compelling them to support such activities with their compelled membership and mandatory dues violated their rights to freedom of speech and association guaranteed by U.S. Const. amend. I and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The dispute was submitted to defendant's arbitration procedures, and plaintiffs, who were dissatisfied with the arbitrator's findings, sought judicial review. After the lower court concluded that plaintiffs' exclusive remedy was under defendant's arbitration procedure and dismissed the action, plaintiffs appealed. In reversing, the court concluded that defendant's arbitration procedures did not preclude adjudication in a judicial forum of plaintiffs' action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claiming violation of U.S. Const. amend. I rights. The court noted that defendant's arbitration procedures were not voluntary.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the lower court's judgment sustaining defendant state bar's general demurrer and dismissing plaintiffs, members of state bar, action because defendant's arbitration procedures did not preclude plaintiffs from subsequently seeking adjudication of their First Amendment claims in a judicial forum.

 

865 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Bradshaw v. Park


No. B078298.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SIX


29 Cal. App. 4th 1267; 34 Cal. Rptr. 2d 872; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 1091; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8220; 94 Daily Journal DAR 15211



October 27, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Ventura County, No. 126538, John J. Hunter, Judge. * 


* Retired judge of the Ventura Municipal Court sitting under assignment by the Chairperson of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. Costs to respondent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant business owner appealed the special judgment of the Superior Court of Ventura County (California) that entered a judgment for a penalty assessed by plaintiff Labor Commissioner pursuant to the Workers' Compensation Act, Cal. Lab. Code § 3726, against defendant for his failure to obtain workers' compensation insurance in violation of Workers' Compensation Act, Cal. Lab. Code § 3700.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff labor commissioner assessed a monetary penalty against defendant business owner under the Workers' Compensation Act, Cal. Lab. Code § 3726, for his failure to obtain workers' compensation insurance, and a clerk entered judgment. Defendant alleged that § 3726 violated the separation of powers doctrine, due process, and the principle of check. The court held that the entry of judgment against defendant did not offend any constitutional principles and affirmed the judgment. The court held that Cal. Const. art. III, § 3 and Cal. Const. art. VI, § 1 did not prohibit the exercise of "quasi-judicial" functions by an administrative agency. The Workers' Compensation Act authorized plaintiff to adjudicate the penalty imposed on defendant, and the penalty effectuated the agency's primary and legitimate regulatory powers. The principle of check was satisfied because there was an opportunity for judicial review. The clerk's entry of judgment was a ministerial function that did not violate Cal. Const. art. III, § 3 and the principle of check. Finally, defendant was not denied due process because he was notified of his right to a hearing and chose not to contest the penalty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment entered against defendant business owner because the penalty assessed by plaintiff labor commissioner and entered as a judgment by the clerk did not violate the separation of powers doctrine, due process, or the principle of check. An administrative agency was authorized to impose monetary relief so long as it was authorized by statute, effectuated the agency's primary purposes, and was reviewable by the courts.

 

866 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Westwinds Mobile Home Park v. Mobilehome Park Rental Review Bd.


No. D017441.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


30 Cal. App. 4th 84; 35 Cal. Rptr. 2d 315; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 1158; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8781; 94 Daily Journal DAR 16209



October 25, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published November 16, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, No. N54104, Thomas Ray Murphy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed. Respondent shall bear costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner of a mobile home park challenged the order of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California) that denied its petition for writ of administrative mandamus and found sufficient evidence supported the order of respondent mobilehome park rental review board that granted a limited rent increase pursuant to a rent control ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Appellant owner of a mobile home park sought a $ 50 rent increase under real party in interest city's rent control ordinance. Respondent mobilehome park rental review board granted an increase of $ 4 per month and appellant filed a petition for writ of administrative mandamus, alleging the order lacked sufficient evidence, and a complaint for declaratory relief. The trial court denied the petition and affirmed the order. Plaintiff sought review. The court reversed, ruling that there was no evidence to support respondent's implicit finding that 2.78 percent was a fair rate of return. Real party in interest had used the "historical cost" approach to measure the rate of return and to produce the 2.78 percent rate. However, there was no evidence that investments in which an investor had a potential for capital appreciation and possible tax shelter benefits provided returns of a similar nature, or that the rate was otherwise appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that denied the petition for writ of administrative mandamus of appellant owner of a mobile home park because there was insufficient evidence to support a conclusion that the order limiting appellant's rent increase provided a fair rate of return. Respondent mobilehome park rental review board was to bear costs on appeal.

 

867 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Chang v. Redding Bank of Commerce


No. C016016.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


29 Cal. App. 4th 673; 35 Cal. Rptr. 2d 64; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 1088; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8231; 94 Daily Journal DAR 15035



October 24, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of San Joaquin County, No. 238588, K. Peter Saiers, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed. Plaintiff shall recover costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner appealed the order of the Superior Court of San Joaquin County that granted summary judgment in favor of defendant bank in plaintiff's action for unjust enrichment and to impose a constructive trust on funds allegedly misappropriated by defendant.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff property owner gave a progress payment to a general contractor to pay subcontractors for work completed on the construction of a hotel. The money was deposited into the general contractor's checking account and checks were issued to the subcontractors. Defendant bank declared a note owed by the general contractor due and set off its claim against the checking account. Defendant returned checks already paid and noted that the checks were paid in error. The trial court granted summary judgment for defendant because plaintiff had no standing as a non-customer to bring an action against defendant. The court reversed and held that a contract between plaintiff and the general contractor created a trust as to the progress payment funds. Accordingly, plaintiff as the settlor had standing to bring the action. The court concluded that there was a triable issue of fact as to whether defendant had actual notice of facts rendering the progress payment a trust fund or if it knew facts that would lead a reasonable person to inquire if the general contractor was acting as a trustee of funds.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order granting summary judgment for defendant bank and held that a contract between plaintiff property owner and a general contractor to use funds as progress payments created a trust. Plaintiff, as settlor of the trust, had standing to bring an action against defendant. The court further held that there was a triable issue of fact as to whether defendant had or should have had notice that the funds were trust money.

Tyler v. Children's Home Society


No. C016382.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


29 Cal. App. 4th 511; 35 Cal. Rptr. 2d 291; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 1068; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8069; 94 Daily Journal DAR 14877



October 21, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied January 5, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 142.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Yolo County, No. 69606, William S. Lebov, Judge. * 


* Judge of the Yolo Municipal Court sitting under assignment by the Chairperson of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the natural parents, appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of Yolo County (California) in favor of defendants, a licensed private adoption agency and its employee, in plaintiffs' action for rescission of their agreements relinquishing their infant child for adoption.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs were two college students who relinquished their baby for adoption. Weeks later, they sought to rescind their relinquishments on grounds that the agreements were void because two of the defendants, a licensed private adoption agency and its employee, failed to comply with state regulations. The trial court ruled in favor of defendants. Plaintiffs appealed. The court found that defendants violated state regulations by failing to discuss placing the baby with extended family, to discuss educational or employment resources, to give plaintiffs copies of the executed documents, and to obtain one plaintiff's medical history. The court concluded that plaintiffs failed to meet their burden of proof to show prejudice from any regulatory violations and therefore failed to prove constructive fraud. As the court found no reversible error or abuse of discretion, it affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court found that plaintiffs, the natural parents, failed to meet their burden of proof to rescind their agreements relinquishing their baby for adoption. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, as it found no reversible error or abuse of discretion.

 

869 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gudger


No. B080311.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


29 Cal. App. 4th 310; 34 Cal. Rptr. 2d 510; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 1055; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7952; 94 Daily Journal DAR 14685



October 18, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. BA076854, Lance A. Ito, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Los Angeles County Superior Court (California), which convicted her of threatening the life of a judge in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 76, arguing that the statute was unconstitutionally overbroad and that the evidence was insufficient to support her conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of threatening the life of a judge in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 76. Defendant appealed, arguing the statute was unconstitutionally overbroad and asserting the evidence was insufficient to support her conviction. The court held that the statute was not overbroad because it criminalized true threats, and not political hyperbole or jokes. The statute only proscribed threats that were unconditional, immediate and so specific as to convey a gravity of purpose and imminent prospect of being carried through, and did not prohibit speech protected by U.S. Const. amend. I. The court found that substantial evidence established that defendant intended her threats to be taken as true threats. Though defendant's threats were conditionally stated, the context in which they were made established that defendant had the specific intent that her statements be taken seriously. Defendant's conviction was, therefore, affirmed.


OUTCOME: Order convicting defendant of threatening the life of a judge was affirmed because the statute criminalized true threats and was not unconstitutionally overbroad; further, sufficient evidence supported defendant's conviction as the context in which defendant made her threats established that she intended her statements be taken seriously.

 

870 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


People v. Dablon


No. D018959.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


39 Cal. App. 4th 284; 34 Cal. Rptr. 2d 761; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 1061; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8038; 94 Daily Journal DAR 14823



October 17, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted January 5, 1995 (S043524), Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 118.
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cites 29 Cal. App. 4th 454 and 34 Cal. App. 4th 372.)]
Review dismissed January 18, 1996 and cause remanded to Ct. App., 4th Dist., Div. 1 (rule 29.4(c), Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1996 Cal. LEXIS 367.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, No. 136063, William H. Kennedy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant criminal appealed his conviction and sentence from the Superior Court of San Diego County (California) on child molestation charges. Defendant claimed his prior acts of child molestation should not have been admitted, the victims should not have been allowed to testify in the presence of a support person, and the sentencing enhancement was improper.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of committing a lewd or lascivious act on a child, Cal. Penal Code § 288(a), (c), and annoying and molesting a child, Cal. Penal Code § 647.6. On appeal, defendant contended that prior acts of child molestation should not have been admitted, that the victims should not have been allowed to testify with a support person present, and that the enhancement sentence should be set aside because the prior charges were not brought and tried separately. The court held prior acts of abuse were properly admitted because they showed the requisite mental state for a lewd or lascivious conviction, established distinctive similarities that satisfied the standard to establish identity, and were not prejudicial because the probative value outweighed the prejudicial effect. The court held the presence of a support person did not prevent a face-to-face confrontation, that the state sufficiently met the standards set forth in Cal. Penal Code § 868.5, and that defendant's failure to object at trial waived the issue for appeal. The court affirmed the conviction and the sentencing enhancement because there was one prior conviction for two crimes tried in a single trial.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed because introduction of prior acts of abuse showed defendant's mental state, established distinctive similarities to show identity, and possessed probative value that outweighed the prejudicial effect. Defendant's failure to object at trial to the use of a support person waived the issue on appeal. The enhanced sentence was affirmed because there were two prior offenses consolidated in one trial.

 

871 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Jenkins


No. B071191.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


29 Cal. App. 4th 287; 34 Cal. Rptr. 2d 483; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 1046; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7931; 94 Daily Journal DAR 14614



October 14, 1994, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts IV A, B, C(2) (a) (b), D and E.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. NA011770, Charles D. Sheldon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of conviction is affirmed. The one-year enhancement for use of a deadly weapon (§ 12022, subd. (b)) is ordered stricken. The cause is remanded for resentencing in conformance with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted him of torture, Cal. Penal Code § 206, mayhem, Cal. Penal Code § 203, assault with a deadly weapon, Cal. Penal Code § 245(a)(1), corporal injury to a cohabitant, Cal. Penal Code § 273.5(a), and possession of a firarm by a felon, Cal. Penal Code § 12021(a). Defendant argued that the trial court erred by not giving a unanimity instruction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for torture, in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 206, challenging the trial court's failure to sua sponte provide the jury with a unanimity instruction. The court held that the trial court only had to instruct the jury on the relevant principles of law raised by the evidence. The court found that a jury instruction on unanimity was not required because the case fell within the continuous course of conduct exception. Defendant's various acts were repetitive, occurred over a period of time, and were thus continuing in nature. Though the individual acts may not have amounted to torture, the cumulative effect was illegal. Because the continuous course of conduct exception applied to the torture charge, the trial court did not err in failing to give an instruction on unanimity. Defendant's conviction was affirmed, and the case was remanded for resentencing after the court struck an enhancement allegation.


OUTCOME: The order convicting defendant of torture was affirmed because the trial court was not required to give a unanimity instruction to the jury; the torture charge fell into the continuous course of conduct exception because the acts constituting torture occurred over a period of time, were repetitive, and had a cumulative illegal effect. As a sentencing enhancement was struck, the case was remanded for resentencing.

Boccato v. City of Hermosa Beach


No. B069256.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR.


29 Cal. App. 4th 1797; 35 Cal. Rptr. 2d 282; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 1148; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8697; 94 Daily Journal DAR 16089



October 14, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published November 14, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. BC034216, Robert H. O'Brien, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed except as to appellants' second cause of action, as to which the judgment is reversed. Each side to bear its own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, store owners, sought review of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which dismissed their action challenging an ordinance for nuisance abatement enacted by respondent city. Appellants claimed the ordinance, which required appellants to obtain a conditional use permit, was unconstitutional because it violated Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 23790(a)(b), Cal. Civ. Code § 52.1, and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, store owners, sought review of the lower court's dismissal of their claim alleging respondent city's enactment of an ordinance, which required them to obtain conditional use permits in order to continue to sell alcoholic beverages, was preempted by state law and violated Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 23790(a), (b), Cal. Civ. Code § 52.1, and 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The record revealed that the ordinance was directed at nuisance abatement. The court held that § 23790(a), (b) exempted from zoning ordinances those stores that predated the enactment of the ordinance if they retained the same type of license and the premises operated continuously. Because appellants met these exceptions, the court reversed the grant of summary judgment on appellants' second cause of action. The court affirmed the dismissal as to § 52.1 and § 1983 because appellants failed to allege violations of the rights of the protected classes set forth in the statutes and failed to claim that the alleged deprivation was committed by a person acting under color of state law.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment for respondent city was reversed in part. Appellants, store owners, could not be required to obtain a conditional use permit because they retained the same type of license and operated continuously. The judgment was otherwise affirmed because appellants failed to allege the type of rights violations covered by statute.

In re Juan C.


No. B073351.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


28 Cal. App. 4th 1093; 33 Cal. Rptr. 2d 919; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 1001; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7546; 94 Daily Journal DAR 13817



September 30, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied January 5, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 135.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. NJ03416, Anthony S. Jones, Commissioner.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant minor sought review of a ruling from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which determined that the allegations made in the state's petition, filed under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 602, as to appellant's violation of a curfew ordinance, Long Beach, Cal., Mun. Code, §§ 2.69.030, 2.69.060. 2.69.070 (1992), were true, and that appellant was properly adjudged a ward of the state, and placed on home probation.


OVERVIEW: Appellant minor sought review of a determination that he had violated a municipal ordinance establishing a curfew, Long Beach, Cal., Mun. Code, §§ 2.69.030, 2.69.060. 2.69.070 (1992), and on appeal challenged the curfew on constitutional grounds. the city had enacted the curfew ordinance in response to civil unrest that included rioting, looting, and arson, the violation of which was a misdemeanor. Appellant claimed that the ordinance was facially overbroad and unconstitutionally restricted various rights and liberties, including the right to travel, the right to associate, the right to assemble, and the right to free speech, as protected under U.S. Const. amends. I, V, and XIV. The court affirmed the lower court determination, holding that the curfew regulation was properly enacted by the municipality by its authority under Cal. Gov't Code § 8634, and that the ordinance did not offend constitutional precepts because the restrictions imposed relative to outdoor assembly between the hours of 7 P.M. and 6 A.M. were reasonably related to a compelling government interest of ensuring the safety and welfare of persons and property in the municipality.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment finding appellant minor in violation of a curfew ordinance, ruling that appellant was not exempt from the operation of the curfew ordinance. The court also ruled that the curfew ordinance was constitutional, rejecting claims that it was vague or overbroad, and that it lent itself to arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement.

Rifkind & Sterling, Inc. v. Rifkind


No. B074042.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


28 Cal. App. 4th 1282; 33 Cal. Rptr. 2d 828; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 979; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7437; 94 Daily Journal DAR 13621



September 28, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied December 22, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Cal. LEXIS 6851.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angles County, No. BC047024, Brett C. Klein, Judge.* * 


* Judge of the Municipal Court for the Los Angeles Judicial District sitting under assignment by the Chairperson of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. The request for sanctions is denied. Plaintiff shall recover costs, including attorney fees, on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant attorney appealed an order from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which confirmed an arbitration award in favor of plaintiff law firm, including punitive damages, in plaintiff's suit for breach of contract. The trial court found that the arbitrator had not exceeded his powers in awarding punitive damages under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1286.6(b), or under the Due Process Clause, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff law firm brought suit against defendant attorney for breach of contract in connection with the firm's dissolution. The contract contained a broadly worded arbitration clause. The suit was stayed pending arbitration, where plaintiff was awarded compensatory damages, attorney fees, and punitive damages. The trial court confirmed the award and defendant appealed, contending that lack of judicial review of punitive damages violated his due process rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1. The court, however, affirmed, finding that the arbitrator had not exceeded his powers under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1286.6(b), that U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1, did not control private arbitration proceedings because they did not constitute state action, and that judicial enforcement of the arbitrator's punitive damage award did not, as a matter of due process, need to include judicial review of the merits of the award. The court denied plaintiff's request for sanctions but awarded plaintiff costs and attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment confirming the arbitration award in favor of plaintiff law firm in its breach of contract suit against defendant attorney, and denied plaintiff's request for sanctions but awarded plaintiff costs and attorney fees. The court held that lack of judicial review of punitive damages awarded in arbitration did not violate due process because the arbitrator's ruling did not constitute state action.

People v. Guinn


No. E012326.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


28 Cal. App. 4th 1130; 33 Cal. Rptr. 2d 791; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 978; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7447; 94 Daily Journal DAR 13637



September 26, 1994, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts I.A, II.A, B, and C and III. under Discussion.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified October 11, 1994. Review Denied January 4, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 17. Review Denied January 5, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 149.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Riverside County, No. CR38392, Ronald R. Heumann, Judge.



DISPOSITION: None of defendant Guinn's contentions has merit. The judgment as to defendant Guinn is affirmed. The judgment as to defendant Johnson is also affirmed; his sentence on the robbery count must be stayed pursuant to Penal Code section 654, and the trial court is directed to issue an amended abstract of judgment staying the robbery count and to provide a copy of the amended abstract to the Department of Corrections.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the Superior Court of Riverside County (California), which convicted defendant of murder, found the special circumstance was true, and imposed a life sentence without possibility of parole.


OVERVIEW: The victim was bludgeoned to death and defendant juvenile was convicted, as an adult, of murder. The trial court found that the murder occurred during a robbery and imposed a life sentence without possibility of parole. Defendant sought review and contended that the special circumstance robbery murder finding under Cal. Penal Code § 190.5 constituted cruel and unusual punishment under U.S. Const. amend. VIII and violated due process under amend. XIV. He also argued that the trial court erred when it denied a jury trial for the penalty phase and that the life sentence was disproportionately severe. The court affirmed. It found that Cal. Penal Code § 190.5 was not unconstitutional because the statutory guidelines, which gave a judge discretion to consider mitigation and aggravation, were not arbitrary and capricious and did not violate due process. The court found that a jury was not appropriate for the penalty phase because under Cal. Penal Code § 190.5, the court, and not a jury, had the power to exercise discretion in a special circumstances murder. Finally, the sentence was not disproportionately severe either to defendant's crime or his personal culpability.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for murder because the sentencing statute did not violate the prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment, because the trial court did not err when it denied a jury for the penalty phase, and because the sentence was not disproportionately severe.

 

876 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hart


No. C017875.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


29 Cal. App. 4th 560; 34 Cal. Rptr. 2d 540; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 1072; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8068; 94 Daily Journal DAR 14901



September 23, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published October 21, 1994. Review Dismissed March 23, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 2150.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Lassen County, No. CR23957, Joseph B. Harvey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Lassen County (California), which convicted him of selling methamphetamine in violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11379. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in ordering him, as a condition of probation, to pay restitution to the county for the cost of the controlled drug buy that resulted in his conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of selling methamphetamine in violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11379. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in ordering him, as a condition of probation, to repay the county the sum it expended in the controlled drug buy that resulted in defendant's conviction because the county was not a victim of his crime. The court disagreed. Under Cal. Penal Code § 1203.04,(a)(l), defendant was required to make restitution to the victim as a condition of probation The policies of Cal. Penal Code §§ 1203.1 and 1203.04 favored a definition of "victim" that included the government if it suffered loss flowing from a defendant's criminal conduct. In this case, the county incurred an actual loss due to the unlawful acts of defendant. The existence of a civil remedy under Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11501 did not preclude such an order of restitution because the civil remedy was not intended as an exclusive one. Accordingly, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant of selling methamphetamine and the condition of probation requiring defendant to pay restitution to the county for the cost of the controlled drug buy that resulted in his conviction. Restitution was a required condition of probation, and a government entity was properly considered a victim of defendant's unlawful act.

People v. Crow


No. E012074.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


28 Cal. App. 4th 440; 33 Cal. Rptr. 2d 624; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 934; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7219; 94 Daily Journal DAR 13203



September 19, 1994, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of part C.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Riverside County, No. CR-40267, W. Charles Morgan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction by the Superior Court of Riverside County (California), for committing lewd and lascivious acts on the body of his 13 year old stepdaughter, in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 288(a) and for possession of a short-barreled shotgun, in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 12020(a).


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant on three of eight identical counts of committing lewd and lascivious acts on the body of his 13-year-old stepdaughter. On appeal he argued among other things: (1) that he was deprived of his constitutional right to have his guilt decided by a unanimous jury as it was impossible to know if the jurors had unanimously agreed on the same three counts, and (2) that the trial court erred when it permitted the state to impeach him with evidence revealed in the course of plea negotiations. The appellate court affirmed the conviction. The court noted that the jury was instructed concerning the necessity of unanimity and was presumed to have complied absent evidence to the contrary. The court held that even in the case of a resident child molester in which the only evidence presented by the state is of a series of separate but indistinguishable acts, the unanimity instruction is sufficient to protect a defendant's right to a unanimous jury so long as there is substantial evidence to support the convictions. The court held that evidence revealed in plea negotiations can be used to impeach, even if it can not be used in the prosecution's case-in-chief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction on three of eight identical counts of committing lewd and lascivious acts on the body of his 13-year-old stepdaughter. The court ruled that the unanimity instruction given the jury protected defendant's right to a unanimous conviction so long as substantial evidence supported it. The court held that evidence obtained during plea negotiations could be used for impeachment purposes.

Freeman & Mills, Inc. v. Belcher Oil Co.


No. B069559.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


33 Cal. App. 4th 837; 33 Cal. Rptr. 2d 585; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 921; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7103; 94 Daily Journal DAR 12926



September 12, 1994, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted December 12, 1994 (S042831) issues limited to whether a party to a contract may recover in tort for another party's bad faith denial of the contract's existence (rule 29.2(b), Cal. Rules of Ct.).
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court. (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cite 28 Cal. App. 4th 282.)] (See 11 Cal. 4th 85)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. C740915, Edward Y. Kakita, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and the cause is remanded to the trial court with directions to retry the issue of damages on Freeman & Mills's breach of contract cause of action only and, when a final judgment is later rendered, to enter judgment in favor of Belcher Oil on Freeman & Mills's "bad faith denial of contract" cause of action. The order denying Freeman & Mills' motion to amend to add a fraud cause of action is affirmed. Freeman & Mills's request for sanctions payable by Belcher Oil for a frivolous appeal is denied. Belcher Oil is awarded its costs of appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff accountants appealed the decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied its request to amend the complaint to add a cause of action for fraud to its breach of contract claims against defendant company. Defendant appealed the trial court's correction of the jury's damage award and an award for the tort of bad faith denial of contract.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff accountants filed a complaint against defendant company alleging breach of contract, bad faith denial of contract, and quantum meruit in connection with an unpaid bill for accounting services. After a jury verdict in plaintiffs' favor, the trial court corrected the jury's damage awards for compensatory and punitive damages on plaintiffs' motion. Defendant appealed the trial court's judgment, alleging that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to correct the damages and that the award of damages for the tort of bad faith denial of contract was improper. Plaintiff appealed the trial court's refusal to permit an amendment of the complaint to add a cause of action for fraud. The court held that the trial court erred in correcting the judgment where there was no clerical error and the judgment conformed to the jury's verdict. The court also determined that the award of punitive damages for the tort of bad faith denial of a contract was improper because there was no special relationship between the parties indicative of unequal bargaining positions. The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded for a new trial on the limited issue of breach of contract damages.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment in favor of plaintiff accountants, holding that the trial court erred in correcting the jury's award where there was no clerical error and that the award of tort damages for bad faith denial of contract was improper where there was no special relationship between the parties. The court remanded for a limited new trial on the issue of breach of contract damages.

 

879 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Silva


No. F019909.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


27 Cal. App. 4th 1160; 33 Cal. Rptr. 2d 181; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 869; 94 Daily Journal DAR 12069



August 26, 1994, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of part 1.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Fresno County, No. 479929-2, A. Dennis Caeton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of Fresno County (California) that convicted him of two counts of spousal abuse and four counts of spousal rape and sentenced him.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of two counts of spousal abuse, Cal. Penal Code § 273.5 and four counts of spousal rape, Cal. Penal Code § 262. Defendant claimed that Cal. Penal Code § 273.5 unconstitutionally discriminated against persons like himself because it excluded from its scope persons who did the same thing to persons of the same sex. The reviewing court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court found that the statute was not subject to strict scrutiny merely because it was a criminal law that could result in incarceration. Rather, the rational basis test applied. Because the state had an interest in preventing domestic violence in opposite-sex relationships, the omission of same-sex relationships from Cal. Penal Code § 273.5 did not render the statute so irrational or invidiously discriminatory as to be unconstitutional. The court concluded that the legislature did not have to choose between attacking every aspect of the problem of domestic violence or not attacking the problem at all.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction because the spousal abuse statute did not violate equal protection merely because it omitted same-sex relationships from its regulation. Equal protection did not require the legislature to regulate all aspects of a problem.

 

880 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Browne v. Russell


No. B078417.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


27 Cal. App. 4th 1116; 33 Cal. Rptr. 2d 29; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 867; 94 Daily Journal DAR 12000



August 25, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing September 20, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 937.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. BC086298, Robert H. O'Brien, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed with directions to enter judgment denying the petition for writ of mandate. As the parties have entered into a joint stipulation of dismissal, we need not award costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city clerk and others sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which issued a writ of mandate that declared unconstitutional an ordinance regulating circulators of referendary petitions in an action brought by respondent restaurants, tobacco manufacturers, and others.


OVERVIEW: After a city published an ordinance prohibiting smoking in restaurants, respondents, a group of restaurants, tobacco manufacturers and others, attempted to qualify a referendum to repeal the ordinance. However, appellant city clerk determined that the petition did not have the required number of qualified signatures because the persons who had circulated portions of the petition were not city residents and registered voters, as required by municipal ordinance. Respondents filed a petition for a writ of mandate. The trial court issued a writ and ordered that no signatures were to be disqualified because of the ordinance. On appeal, the court reversed. Although the circulation of initiative petitions involved core political speech, respondents failed to show that the residency and registration requirements of the ordinance limited the opportunity of city residents and voters to hear about and discuss the petition. Moreover, the city had a compelling interest in the integrity of the referendum process that the ordinance protected. Charter cities could provide for the exercise of the power of referendum in any manner that did not impinge on the basic right of referendum.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that granted the petition for a writ of mandate brought by respondent restaurants, tobacco manufacturers, and others. The court held that the residency and voter registration requirements for persons who circulated ordinances did not unduly burden respondents' right of political expression and protected the referendum process from special interests.
