City of Berkeley v. City of Berkeley Rent Stabilization Bd.


No. A059403.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


27 Cal. App. 4th 951; 33 Cal. Rptr. 2d 317; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 829; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6189; 94 Daily Journal DAR 11283



August 12, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Alameda County, Nos. 683721-5 and 683726-0, John Sutter, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The ruling of the trial court is affirmed in all respects, except for its ruling that the regulations in issue are inapplicable to post-1979 landlord purchasers. The latter ruling is reversed. The matter is remanded to the trial court, with instructions to issue a judgment denying the petition for writ of mandate in its entirety. Costs on appeal are awarded to the Board and to Berkeley Property Owners' Association.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervener landlord's group sought review of a portion of a judgment from Superior Court of Alameda County (California), rejecting defendant, rent stabilization board's, grant of inflation adjustments to post-1979 purchasers of property. Plaintiff city filed a timely cross-appeal from the court's judgment upholding actions of defendant rent stabilization board in enacting rent control regulations.


OVERVIEW: Defendant rent stabilization board enacted regulations providing for an increase in rent levels and for future annual general adjustments to rent. The regulations were applicable to all rental units regardless of purchase date. Certain below-market rent levels were permitted to be raised. Certain adjustments to rent were permitted on an annual basis by defendant. Plaintiffs, tenant's organization and city, challenged these regulations and contended that defendant's actions were in excess of defendant's authority. The trial court rejected defendant's grant of inflation adjustments to rental properties purchased after 1979 but upheld all other aspects of implemented regulations as within defendant's power. Plaintiff city appealed judgment upholding regulations. Defendants board and intervener property owners association appealed the denial of regulations' applicability to post-1979 purchasers. The reviewing court found no prejudicial abuse of discretion. Defendant's actions were consistent with its authority and consistent with case law determinations. Judgment holding regulations were inapplicable to post-1979 purchasers was reversed and the remainder of judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Ruling that regulations implemented by defendant city rent stabilization board were inapplicable to post-1979 landlord purchasers was reversed. Ruling upholding all other regulations was affirmed. Defendant did not act outside the scope of its power or abuse its discretion in implementing regulations. The matter was remanded to the trial court with instructions to issue judgment denying a petition for writ of mandate in its entirety.

 

882 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



In re Autumn H.


No. D020708.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


27 Cal. App. 4th 567; 32 Cal. Rptr. 2d 535; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 816; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6084; 94 Daily Journal DAR 11097



August 8, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied October 27, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Cal. LEXIS 5777.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, No. 507193, Peter E. Riddle, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which, at the request of respondent San Diego County Department of Social Services, changed the permanent plan of appellant's dependent daughter from long-term foster care to adoption and terminated appellant's parental rights under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 366.26.


OVERVIEW: Appellant father's children were taken into protective custody after appellant kicked one of them, causing injuries. The children were then declared dependents of the trial court for the second time and were placed with their grandparents or in foster homes. Appellant was incarcerated during most of the first six months of reunification and upon release entered a residential alcohol rehabilitation facility. He visited the children on a weekly basis. The trial court continued appellant's reunification services for a time, but ultimately found that the youngest daughter was adoptable, severed appellant's parental rights, and referred the daughter for adoptive placement. Appellant sought review of the decision. The court affirmed the trial court's order. The court held that the statutory exception to placement for adoption where a benefit from continuing the parent/child relationship was found, under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 366.26(c)(1)(A), was clear and not violative of appellant's right to due process and that substantial evidence supported the order terminating appellant's parental rights and freeing the daughter for adoption.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order terminating appellant father's parental rights and changing his daughter's permanent plan from long-term foster care to adoption because substantial evidence supported the order and because a statutory exception providing that adoptive placement be foregone where there was a benefit to the child from continuing the parent/child relationship was not unconstitutionally vague.

 

883 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



In re Andrew S.


No. B063908.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


27 Cal. App. 4th 541; 32 Cal. Rptr. 2d 670; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 814; 94 Daily Journal DAR 11047; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6081



August 5, 1994, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts I, II and IV of Discussion.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified on Denial of Rehearing September 2, 1994. Review Denied October 20, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Cal. LEXIS 5602.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. J982004, Martha Bellinger, Temporary Judge. * 


* Pursuant to California Constitution, article VI, section 21.



DISPOSITION: For the foregoing reasons, the judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which terminated her parental rights to her four minor children. Appellant claimed that she had been wrongfully deprived of counsel at a permanency planning hearing held pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 366.26.


OVERVIEW: At a permanency planning hearing held pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 366.26, at which appellant mother was not present and without any prior notice, appellant's counsel's request to be relieved was granted. Appellant's parental rights were subsequently terminated at the conclusion of the hearing. The appellate court affirmed. Pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 317(d), appellant had the right to be represented at the hearing. However, that right was not of constitutional dimension at a § 366.26 hearing because at that stage of the proceedings it had already been determined that appellant could not have custody of her children. Because the right to counsel was statutory, the trial court's error in depriving appellant of an attorney at the hearing could not require reversal unless prejudice was shown pursuant to Cal. Const. art. VI, § 13. The appellate court determined that there was no prejudice shown, and any error was harmless because the facts established that the trial court was amply justified in deciding that adoption was in the children's best interests, and the result would not have been different even if counsel was appointed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the order that terminated appellant mother's parental rights because, although the trial court erred by depriving appellant of counsel during a permanency planning hearing, the error was not reversible per se and was harmless in any event where the circumstances were such that counsel being present could not have changed the outcome of the hearing.

 

884 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Kenneally v. Medical Board


No. B075024.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


27 Cal. App. 4th 489; 32 Cal. Rptr. 2d 504; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 802; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6036; 94 Daily Journal DAR 10965



August 4, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing August 23, 1994. Review Denied October 13, 1994 (S032839), Reported at: 1994 Cal. LEXIS 5455.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. BC078273, Robert H. O'Brien, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order issuing a preliminary injunction is reversed. Respondents shall bear appellants' costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Medical Board of California sought reversal of the order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County, issuing a preliminary injunction against appellant and enjoining it from going forward with respondent physician's disciplinary proceedings until respondent had the opportunity to take the depositions that he requested.


OVERVIEW: Appellant Medical Board of California filed an accusation against respondent physician for gross negligence and incompetence. A disciplinary hearing was scheduled and respondent noticed several depositions, which appellant informed were not authorized. Respondent filed a complaint for declaratory and injunctive relief in superior court alleging that the Administrative Procedure Act, Cal. Gov't Code § 11511, denied him equal protection by restricting prehearing depositions in disciplinary proceedings to witnesses whose testimony was material and who were unable to attend the hearing, when such depositions were not similarly restricted in attorney disciplinary proceedings. The trial court found in favor of respondent and issued a preliminary injunction, and appellant sought reversal. The court reversed the ruling of the superior court and concluded that a physician had no fundamental right to continue to practice his or her profession. Therefore, the court applied the rational basis test rather than the strict scrutiny test, and found that Cal. Gov't Code § 11511 had a rational basis, as the state had an interest in swiftly and expeditiously disciplining physicians.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the superior court and held that the Administrative Procedure Act did not violate respondent physician's equal protection right by denying him the opportunity to depose witnesses in preparation for his administrative disciplinary hearing. Respondent did not have a fundamental right to practice medicine, and the statute had a rational basis in the state's interest in streamlining the procedure.

 

885 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Angeles Electric Co. v. Superior Court


No. B078927.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


27 Cal. App. 4th 426; 32 Cal. Rptr. 2d 660; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 798; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6002; 94 Daily Journal DAR 10922



August 3, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied November 3, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Cal. LEXIS 6001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. BC 043122, Stephen Lachs, Judge.



DISPOSITION: We conclude that the payments by Buckley to Angeles which are the subject of the summary adjudication reviewed in this case are recoverable preferences by the assignee for benefit of creditors. The trial court ruled correctly in so deciding. We therefore dissolve the alternative writ and stay, previously issued, and deny petitioner's application for a peremptory writ.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review by prerogative writ of the order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), granting summary judgment in favor of plaintiff, assignee for benefit of creditors in his attempt to set aside a payment made by a debtor to petitioner for construction materials.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, subcontractor, furnished materials for a construction project and placed a mechanics lien on the owner's property. Debtor, petitioner's general contractor, paid petitioner for the materials, and petitioner furnished debtor with a release of the mechanics lien recognizing the amount paid. Debtor assigned the release of the mechanic's lien for benefit of creditors to assignee who instituted an action against petitioner to set aside the payment by debtor to petitioner. In an affirmative defense, petitioner asserted that the release of the mechanics lien, in exchange for payment for materials previously furnished to the project for which compensation was due and unpaid, constituted a contemporaneous exchange for new value, and was not subject to avoidance by plaintiff. The trial court granted summary judgment to plaintiff and concluded that the release of the mechanic's lien was not an exchange for new value, as required by the preference exemption, Cal. Code Civ. Proc. § 1800 (c)(1)(A). The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and held that the payments made by debtor to petitioner were recoverable preferences by the assignee for benefit of creditors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment because the release of the mechanics lien, in exchange for payment for materials previously furnished to the project for which compensation was due and unpaid, was not a contemporaneous exchange for new value, and was not subject to avoidance by plaintiff. The payments made by debtor to petitioner were recoverable preferences by the assignee for benefit of creditors.

 

886 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



KGTV Channel 10 v. Superior Court


No. D021046.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


26 Cal. App. 4th 1673; 32 Cal. Rptr. 2d 181; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 763; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5651; 94 Daily Journal DAR 10293; 23 Media L. Rep. 1303



July 21, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of San Diego County, No. 169963, William C. Pate, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner media representatives filed a petition for writ of mandate regarding an order of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which ordered petitioners not to disclose the name or likeness of the minor in connection with a detention hearing in juvenile court where the minor had been charged with murder. The juvenile court issued an order directing one of the petitioners to show cause why it should not be held in contempt.


OVERVIEW: A minor was arrested and charged with murder and her full name and image were broadcast by the media at her arrest a few days before a detention hearing in juvenile court. The juvenile court allowed the press to stay at the hearing, issuing a minute order prohibiting them from disclosing the name or likeness of the minor in connection with the hearing. The minor's name and footage from her arrest was broadcast with a story about the murder. The juvenile court issued an order directing one of petitioner media representatives to show cause why it should not have been held in contempt. On appeal, the court vacated the juvenile court's minute order and its order to show cause regarding contempt. The court held that murder was one of the serious offenses that opened the door to a public hearing under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code §§ 676(a), (b). Petitioners had a statutory right to attend the hearing and a constitutional right to say what transpired. Where petitioners learned the minor's name at the detention hearing and saw for themselves that she was the same person arrested and pictured earlier, they had a right to report the information free from any restraint by the juvenile court.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the juvenile court's minute order prohibiting petitioner media representatives from disclosing the name or likeness of the minor charged with murder in connection with a juvenile detention hearing. The court also vacated the juvenile court's order directing one of petitioners to show cause regarding contempt. Petitioners had a statutory right to attend the hearing and a constitutional right to say what transpired.

 

887 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Jones v. Superior Court


No. D021024.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


26 Cal. App. 4th 1202; 31 Cal. Rptr. 2d 890; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 745; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5539; 94 Daily Journal DAR 10117



July 19, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of San Diego County, No. CR136371, Laura P. Hammes, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant murderer challenged an order from the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), that denied appellant's counsel's request for the addresses and telephone number of eight jurors, whom requested that such information not be disclosed, on the ground that the disclosure statute, Cal Civ. Proc. Code § 206, was an unconstitutional invasion of the jurors' right to privacy, and that it prohibited any contact with those jurors.


OVERVIEW: After appellant murderer was sentenced to death, the trial court, after hearing, refused to release addresses and telephone numbers of eight jurors that objected to that information being releasing to appellant's counsel, and it issued a no contact order that prohibited appellant's counsel or their investigators from contacting those eight jurors. The appellate court affirmed. The appellate court observed that Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 206 protected jurors from unwanted postverdict intrusions by giving them an absolute right to not discuss deliberations or the verdict with anyone, Cal Civ. Proc. Code § 206(a), and requiring their consent before contact. Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 206(b). Further, Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 237 strengthened juror protections by permitting sealing juror information after a criminal case when there was a compelling governmental interest. Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 237(b). The appellate court held that a juror's refusal to discuss deliberations or the case was a compelling interest sufficient to keep the juror's information sealed, and in that situation Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 207(f) did not apply.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that prohibited appellant's counsel from contacting any juror that exercised the right to not discuss the case or verdict and that withheld consent to contact, and thereby denied appellant's petition for writ of mandate, because after a juror exercised that absolute right there was a continuing compelling governmental interest which authorized keeping juror personal information sealed.

 

888 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Building Industry Assn. v. City of Oceanside


No. D016581.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


27 Cal. App. 4th 744; 33 Cal. Rptr. 2d 137; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 841; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6294



July 19, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published August 16, 1994 on Denial of Rehearing, Reported at: 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 874.
Review Denied October 13, 1994 (S041754), Reported at: 1994 Cal. LEXIS 5500.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, No. N37638, Herbert B. Hoffman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed with directions to enter judgment in favor of BIA on the grounds that Prop. A impermissibly conflicts with the City's general plan and with Government Code sections 65008, 65913.1, and 65915. Each party to bear its own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant building association challenged the decision of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which entered judgment in respondent city's favor in a three-phase court trial on appellant's complaint as to the validity of a residential growth control initiative, adopted by the voters of respondent.


OVERVIEW: The trial court entered judgment, in appellant building association's action, that respondent city's residential growth control initiative, known as Proposition A, was valid. In reviewing the action, the court declined to base its decision on whether the trial court properly interpreted Cal. Evid. Code § 669.5(b), as requiring respondent to show only that Proposition A was reasonably related to the public health, safety, and welfare, as opposed to showing it was "necessary" to promote those objectives. Instead the court held that the dispositive issue presented was whether Proposition A impermissibly conflicted with either respondent's general plan or state law provisions litigated at trial. The court reversed the judgment, holding that Proposition A was facially in conflict with respondent's general plan and with state planning and zoning law. The court held that a zoning ordinance that conflicts with a general plan is invalid at the time it is passed. The court further held that the court did not invalidate the ordinance, but only determined the existence of the conflict. It is the preemptive effect of the controlling state statute which invalidated the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment, in favor of appellant building association, because respondent city's Proposition A was facially in conflict with respondent's general plan and with state planning and zoning law.

 

889 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Billester v. City of Corona


No. E011320


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


26 Cal. App. 4th 1107; 32 Cal. Rptr. 2d 121; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 730; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5450; 94 Daily Journal DAR 9958



July 13, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied October 12, 1994 (S041570), Reported at: 1994 Cal. LEXIS 5387.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Riverside County, No. 214970, Ronald T. Deissler, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, minor and parents, sought review of a judgment entered by the Court of Appeal of California, Fourth Appellate District, Division Two, which affirmed the dismissal of plaintiffs' action against defendant city for damages sustained by plaintiff minor in an automobile accident.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff minor was injured when the vehicle he was a passenger in was broadsided by a vehicle driven by a suspect that was fleeing from one of defendant city's police officers. Plaintiffs, minor and his parents, filed suit against defendant to recover damages for plaintiff minor's injuries. The trial court determined that defendant was immune from liability because it adopted a pursuit policy that complied with the immunity provisions of Cal. Veh. Code § 17004.7. The appellate court affirmed. The court also affirmed, concluding that defendant's policy complied with § 17004.7, and that plaintiffs' suit was thus barred, because it provided for supervisory control of the pursuit, it set forth procedures for designating the primary pursuit vehicle and for determining the total number of vehicles permitted to participate in a pursuit, it provided for coordination of operations with other jurisdictions, and it set forth adequate guidelines for initiating and terminating pursuits. The court also concluded that § 17004.7 did not violate plaintiffs' equal protection rights because the legislature had a rational basis for conferring immunity on cities with proper pursuit policies.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court, which dismissed an action brought by plaintiffs, minor and parents, because defendant city adopted a valid police pursuit policy and was thus immune from liability for the injuries sustained by plaintiff minor in an accident that resulted from a police pursuit.

Hill v. Newkirk


No. D017909.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


26 Cal. App. 4th 1047; 31 Cal. Rptr. 2d 859; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 719; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5379; 94 Daily Journal DAR 9799



July 12, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of San Diego County, No. 627156, Barbara T. Gamer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which sustained appellee foster mother's demurrer without leave to amend in appellant's negligence action against appellee for the death of her infant daughter, on the ground that appellant failed to first file a claim under Cal. Health & Safety Code § 1527.6(d).


OVERVIEW: Appellant mother's child was placed with appellee foster mother, a foster parent licensed to care for medically fragile children. The child died while in appellee's care. Eleven months later, appellant filed an administrative claim with the county pursuant to the California Tort Claims Act, Cal. Gov't Code § 905 et seq. The county rejected the claim as untimely. Appellant filed a negligence suit against appellee. The trial court sustained appellee's demurrer without leave to amend, based on appellant's failure to first file a claim with the Foster Family Home and Small Family Home Insurance Fund (Fund) under Cal. Health & Safety Code § 1527.6(d), and appellant sought review. The court affirmed the judgment. The court held that the fact that appellant did not affirmatively allege appellee operated a foster family home or a small family home did not take the case outside the purview of the Fund's claim requirement, and that the claim was precisely the type the Fund was established to cover. The court found no basis upon which to conclude that the filing with the county constituted substantial compliance, and rejected estoppel and constitutional arguments.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court sustaining appellee foster mother's demurrer to appellant mother's suit claiming negligence in the death of her infant daughter, because appellant had failed to first file the required administrative claim.

City of Fresno v. Fresno Firefighters Local 753


No. F018749


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


26 Cal. App. 4th 958; 32 Cal. Rptr. 2d 449; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 724; 146 L.R.R.M. 3007; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5382; 94 Daily Journal DAR 9789



July 11, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified on Denial of Rehearing August 10, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 834.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of Fresno County. Super. Ct. No. 462602-4. Hon. Stephen J. Kane, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant firefighter's unions challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Fresno County, California, which entered a judgment in favor of appellee city in appellee's action for declaratory relief.


OVERVIEW: Appellant firefighter's unions sought review of the trial court's declaratory judgment in favor of appellee city. The trial court held the zipper clauses in the two memoranda of understanding between the parties violated appellee's rights under the California Constitution to propose charter amendments by permitting appellants to decide if appellee could propose a ballot measure to voters concerning the repeal or amendments of the county charter. The court held that if a city must meet and confer on proposed amendments affecting areas subject to the Meyers-Milas-Brown Act, it followed that city could agree to forgo a charter amendment, propose a different amendment, or concur with a proposal that inhibits its ability to change a charger term. Any waiver of the right to propose charter amendments contrary to the terms of the memorialized agreements during the life of the agreements did not waive the electorates separate right to propose and approve charter amendments through the initiative process. The court concluded that because the trial court granted summary judgment based on its conclusion that such agreements were unconstitutional, the order appealed from must be reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order because the trial court erroneously based its summary judgments on the ground that zipper clauses in a memoranda agreement were unconstitutional; however, the court determined that the trial court correctly found that appellee city failed to establish all the facts necessary to justify a judgment in its favor.

City of Fresno v. Fresno Firefighters Local 753

COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT

Smiley v. Citibank


No. B078913.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN.


36 Cal. App. 4th 196; 32 Cal. Rptr. 2d 562; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 710; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5333; 94 Daily Journal DAR 9751



July 11, 1994, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Modified August 11, 1994. Review Granted October 27, 1994 (S041711), Reported at: 1994 Cal. LEXIS 5759.
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cites 21 Cal. App. 4th 572 and 26 Cal. App. 4th 1767 and 31 Cal. App. 4th 1730.)] (See 11 Cal. 4th 138)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. BC059202, Melvin B. Grover, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant credit card account holder sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), that dismissed appellant's claim against respondent bank in a class action for damages and injunctive relief alleging respondent charged excessive late fees on credit cards accounts, on grounds that the fees were impermissible under Cal. Bus. & Prof. § 1671.


OVERVIEW: Appellant credit card account holder brought a class action against respondent bank seeking damages and injunctive relief alleging respondent charged excessive late charges on her and others' credit card accounts and that these fees were impermissible under Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 1671 and common law. Respondent argued that the claims were preempted under federal law. The trial court denied respondent's motion to dismiss but the appellate court issued a writ of mandate and the trial court dismissed appellant's actions. Appellant claimed that 12 U.S.C.S. §§ 85 and 86 governed the amount of interest national banks could charge and that late fees were not interest. The court affirmed the trial court's order and ruled that credit card late charges were interest and governed by §§ 85 and 86 and that state law to regulate these charges was preempted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment dismissing appellant credit card account holder's claim and held that the late charges were governed solely by federal law and that any state law purporting to regulate late charges was preempted.

In re Marriage of Heikes


No. B073297.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SIX


36 Cal. App. 4th 1; 31 Cal. Rptr. 2d 721; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 704; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5297; 94 Daily Journal DAR 9671



July 7, 1994, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Review Granted October 13, 1994 (S041579), Reported at: 1994 Cal. LEXIS 5396.
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cites 26 Cal. App. 4th 830 and 31 Cal. App. 4th 968.)] (See 10 Cal. 4th 1211)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Santa Barbara County, No. 181992, Patrick L. McMahon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, the order granting a new trial is affirmed. Wife shall bear costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wife challenged an order of the Superior Court of Santa Barbara County (California), which partially granted appellee husband's new trial motion as to his right to reimbursement under Cal. Civ. Code § 4800.2 for jointly held real property that he owned before their marriage.


OVERVIEW: Appellant wife sought a divorce from appellee husband, claiming an interest in real property that he owned before their marriage that the parties held as joint tenants. The trial court held that appellant had a one-half interest in the parcels. Appellee then sought a new trial based on his assertion that a very recent California Supreme Court decision permitted retroactive application of Cal. Civ. Code § 4800.2. The trial court granted a partial new trial to give appellee an opportunity to claim reimbursement for his separate property contributions in the real property acquisitions. On review sought by appellant, the court affirmed the grant of a new trial. The court found that appellee's failure to ask the trial court to reject or limit the binding California Supreme Court decision and to specify if his motion rested upon affidavits or the trial court minutes were not fatal to his new trial motion. The court reasoned that the new trial motion rested on application of legal principles that a recent decision declared, and that specification of affidavits or the minutes of the trial court would not have assisted either appellant or the trial court regarding the new trial motion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the partial grant of appellee husband's motion for a new trial in appellant wife's divorce suit as to his right to reimbursement for jointly held property that he owned before their marriage. The court held that errors in filing appellee's motion were not fatal because he relied on recently declared principles, and specifying affidavits or the minutes of the trial court would not have helped appellant or the trial court.

 

895 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


American Academy of Pediatrics v. Lungren


No. A058627.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


40 Cal. App. 4th 255; 32 Cal. Rptr. 2d 546; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 687; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5184; 94 Daily Journal DAR 9477



June 30, 1994, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified July 27, 1994.
Rehearing Denied August 1, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 813. Review Granted September 29, 1994 (S041459), Reported at: 1994 Cal. LEXIS 5332.
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cites 26 Cal. App. 4th 479 and 31 Cal. App. 4th 861 and 35 Cal. App. 4th 1385.)] (See 12 Cal. 4th 1007.)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, No. 884574, Maxine M. Chesney, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment and order of injunction are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged an order of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which enjoined the state's enforcement of Cal. Civ. Code § 34.5, declaring these provisions unconstitutional as violating California's right to privacy.


OVERVIEW: Respondent health care providers challenged the constitutionality of 1987 Cal. Stat. 1237, which provided that an unemancipated minor could not obtain a therapeutic abortion without first having obtained the written consent of a parent or legal guardian, or by petitioning the juvenile court. After the superior court declared the legislation unconstitutional and enjoined the state from enforcing Cal. Civ. Code § 34.5, as amended by 1987 Cal. Stat. 1237, as well as provisions of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 25958, the court remanded for factual determinations regarding whether the legislation burdened the right to privacy. On remand, the superior court held that respondents made a prima facie showing of an unconstitutional invasion of the right of privacy, but that the state failed to show that the burden on the right was justified by the interests which the legislation sought to further. On appeal sought by the state, the court affirmed the judgment and order of injunction, holding that, while the health and welfare of minors is a compelling state interest, the legislation in question did not further this interest, but instead, burdened the fundamental privacy rights of minors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court enjoining the state's implementation of statutory provisions amended by legislation, where the legislation was shown to unconstitutionally impinge on the fundamental privacy rights of minors by requiring them to obtain parental consent prior to an abortion.

 

896 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Golden State Homebuilding Associates v. City of Modesto


Nos. F019643, F019921.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


26 Cal. App. 4th 601; 31 Cal. Rptr. 2d 572; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 684; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5155; 94 Daily Journal DAR 9505



June 30, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied September 15, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Cal. LEXIS 5090.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Stanislaus County, No. 286093, Aldo Girolami, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed. Costs are awarded to the City and County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city and county, appealed an order of the Superior Court of Stanislaus County (California), which held that plaintiff developers were entitled to a declaration that impact fees conditioned on the issuance of building permits violated Cal. Gov't Code § 65961 and a peremptory writ mandating that defendants issue the permits and refund fees already paid.


OVERVIEW: Defendant city approved a tentative map, giving plaintiff developers a vested right to proceed with development of a residential subdivision. Six weeks later, defendant city agreed to collect fees for defendant county. After the final map was approved and plaintiffs' rights expired, defendant city refused to issue building permits unless plaintiffs paid capital and public facilities fees. The trial court granted judgment for plaintiffs declaring that the fees violated Cal. Gov't Code § 65961 and a peremptory writ mandating the issuance of permits and the refund of fees already paid on 26 units. Both parties appealed. The court reversed and awarded costs to defendants. The court held that because defendant city could not have lawfully imposed a condition requiring payment of impact fees in the future, it was not barred by § 65961 from subsequently imposing the condition on permits. The court held that any due process right to develop free of fees did not vest until issuance of the permits. The court denied plaintiffs' cross-appeal because they were estopped by their stipulations from seeking the expansion of the ruling to all units.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment in favor of plaintiff developers and awarded costs to defendants, city and county. The court held that defendant city was not barred from conditioning impact fees on the issuance of building permits when it could not have lawfully conditioned its approval of a tentative map on plaintiff developers' payment of fees in the future.

Broadmoor Police Protection Dist. v. San Mateo Local Agency Formation Com.


No. A060343.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


26 Cal. App. 4th 304; 31 Cal. Rptr. 2d 536; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 670; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5067; 94 Daily Journal DAR 9299



June 29, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 27, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 788. Review Denied September 29, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Cal. LEXIS 5341.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Mateo County, No. 363184, Harlan K. Veal, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a police protection unit, sought review of an order of the Superior Court of San Mateo County (California) ruling in favor of respondents, a city and a county local agency formation commission, regarding the constitutionality of the protest provisions involving municipal and county service area reorganizations and annexations contained in the Cortese-Knox Local Government Reorganization Act of 1985, Cal. Gov't Code § 56000 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Respondents, a city and county local agency formation commission, annexed land that was uninhabited and appellant, a police protection unit, filed suit challenging the constitutionality of the protest provisions involving municipal and county service area reorganizations and annexations contained in the Cortese-Knox Local Government Reorganization Act of 1985, Cal. Gov't Code § 56000 et seq. The trial court ruled in favor of respondents and appellant sought review. Appellant contended that the mechanism for determining a majority protest under the statute violated the equal protection clauses of the state and federal constitutions. The court concluded that the procedure for majority protest by landowners in uninhabited territories, based on the assessed value of their land as set forth in Cal Gov't. Code § 57078(a), was rationally related to a number of legitimate governmental purposes under the rational basis test. The protest procedure set forth in § 57078(a) was, therefore, constitutional. The court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of respondents, a city and county local agency formation commission, regarding the constitutionality of the protest provisions in the Cortese-Knox Local Government Reorganization Act of 1985. The court held that the procedure for majority protest by landowners in uninhabited territories, based on the assessed value of their land, was rationally related to legitimate governmental purposes.

Rezai v. City of Tustin


No. G013648.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


26 Cal. App. 4th 443; 31 Cal. Rptr. 2d 559; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 673; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5083; 94 Daily Journal DAR 9310



June 29, 1994, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of part II.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied September 14, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Cal. LEXIS 5054.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Orange County, No. 643703, Thomas N. Thrasher, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. Respondents are entitled to their costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant developer challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Orange County (California), which found in favor of respondent city on appellant's claims for breach of contract, promissory estoppel, various statutory violations, and declaratory relief. Appellant asserted that the trial court erred in awarding judgment to respondent on the pleadings.


OVERVIEW: After a hearing, respondent city granted appellant developer a conditional use permit to construct an apartment project. After construction began, respondent determined that appellant's list of parties omitted several property owners who were entitled to notice. Based on complaints and the inadequate notice, respondent revoked appellant's permit. Eventually, appellant was granted a permit for a significantly scaled back project. Appellant brought an action against respondent for damages arising out of the revocation of the original conditional use permit and building permit. The trial court granted judgment to respondent on the pleadings. On appeal, the court held that the trial court properly dismissed appellant's action on the pleadings because he failed to seek administrative mandamus under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1094.5, before bringing his action for damages. The court held that respondent was not estopped from raising the mandamus requirement for failure to give appellant notice under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code §1094.6(b), because the application of estoppel would not punish respondent but would injure the area residents who could not be held responsible for respondent's mistakes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment granted by the trial court on the pleadings in favor of respondent city in appellant developer's action for money damages resulting from a revoked land use permit. An administrative mandamus was the proper method to challenge the validity of conditions imposed on a building permit, and appellant had failed to pursue this remedy.

 

899 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Higgins


No. G013616.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


26 Cal. App. 4th 247; 31 Cal. Rptr. 2d 516; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 664; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4965; 94 Daily Journal DAR 9130



June 28, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied October 13, 1994 (S041424), Reported at: 1994 Cal. LEXIS 5620.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Orange County, No. C-96662, Richard M. Aronson, Temporary Judge.* * 


* Pursuant to California Constitution, article VI, section 21.



DISPOSITION: The judgments are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of a decision by the Superior Court of Orange County (California), which denied their motions to suppress evidence that was found during a warrantless search of their residence. After the denial of their motions, defendants pleaded guilty to various narcotics offenses.


OVERVIEW: During a domestic disturbance call officers conducted a warrantless search of defendants' residence and found marijuana, cocaine, and a triple beam scale. Defendants pleaded guilty to various narcotics offenses after the trial court denied their motions to suppress the evidence found in the search, because exigent circumstances justified the officers' warrantless entry into defendants' residence. The court found the motions were properly suppressed and affirmed the trial court's judgment. It reasoned that the officers were called to defendants' residence in response to a report of physical violence. When they encountered the female defendant, she was extremely frightened and appeared to be the victim of a felony battery. She also lied about being alone and gave the officers a suspicious story about falling down the stairs. The court reasoned that viewed objectively, the circumstances justified the officers' entry and search of the residence to ensure the female defendant's safety. The court could not say, as a matter of law, that the officers' failure to procure a warrant rendered their actions unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court found that the trial court properly denied defendants' motions to suppress evidence found by police officers during a warrantless search of their residence, and it affirmed the judgment of the trial court that defendants were guilty of various narcotics offenses. It did so because the officers' actions were objectively reasonable and motivated by their concern for the female defendant's well being.

People ex rel. San Francisco Bay Conservation Etc. Com v. Smith


No. A059257.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


26 Cal. App. 4th 113; 31 Cal. Rptr. 2d 488; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 658; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4882; 94 Daily Journal DAR 8863



June 24, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Marin County, No. 138105, Lynn O'Malley Taylor, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed insofar as it denies BCDC injunctive relief against the mooring of Storms's vessel, and the cause is remanded with directions to issue an injunction and consider further relief. The judgment is in all other respects affirmed. Costs on the appeals and cross-appeal go to BCDC.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant vessel owners appealed injunctions issued by the Superior Court of Marin County (California) under the McAteer-Petris Act, Cal. Gov. Code tit. 7.2, § 66600 et seq., against the offshore mooring of certain vessels and respondent San Francisco Bay Conservation and Development Commission appealed the denial of relief against the mooring of one other vessel.


OVERVIEW: Appellant vessel owners filed suit to bar enforcement of a regional agency ordinance which, among other things, prohibited the offshore mooring of residential-use vessels for periods longer than 30 days. Respondent San Francisco Bay Conservation and Development Commission (BCDC) intervened as a defendant to protect its interest in enforcement of the ordinance and its special area plan. The McAteer-Petris Act required permits before persons or entities could have placed fill within areas of the San Francisco Bay Conservation and Development Commission's jurisdiction. The court found an injunction by the lower court in favor of respondent was supported because the vessels were "fill" under the McAteer-Petris Act, Cal. Gov't. Code tit. 7.2, § 66632(a), and moored without required permits from respondent. The court further found there was no evidence that any of the appellants had ceased mooring their vessels or obtained the required permits before judgment. The fact that the vessels were capable of navigation or self-propulsion did not entitle appellants to indefinitely moor the vessels offshore in violation of the statute and without permits.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed insofar as it denied respondent San Francisco Bay Conservation and Development Commission injunctive relief against the mooring of a vessel, and the cause was remanded with directions to issue an injunction and consider further relief. The judgment was in all other respects affirmed because the offshore mooring of the vessels violated statutory provisions.

Stress Care, Inc. v. Workers' Comp. Appeals Bd.


No. B076533.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR.


26 Cal. App. 4th 909; 32 Cal. Rptr. 2d 426; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 748; 94 Daily Journal DAR 9991; 59 Cal. Comp. Cases 388



June 20, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of the Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published July 13, 1994. As Modified July 13, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Proceeding to review a decision of the Workers' Compensation Appeals Board. W.C.A.B. No. MON 147546


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, counselor and clinic, sought review of an order of the Workers' Compensation Appeals Board (California), which denied reconsideration after a workers' compensation judge ordered them to pay a civil penalty to the board for a knowing violation of Cal. Lab. Code § 4628, by submitting a psychological report in an underlying workers' compensation proceeding.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, counselor and clinic, submitted a psychological report in a workers' compensation hearing. Because petitioner counselor was not the health care provider who had examined the injured worker, the workers' compensation judge determined that petitioners had violated Cal. Lab. Code § 4268, 1900 Cal. Stat. ch. 1550, § 34, and assessed a civil penalty of $ 1000. The Workers' Compensation Appeals Board denied reconsideration, and petitioners appealed. The court annulled the board's denial of reconsideration and remanded for further proceedings, holding that petitioner counselor was not a "physician" as defined by Cal. Lab. Code § 3209.3, 1988 Cal. Stat. ch. 1496, § 1. Because petitioner counselor was not a physician, and because petitioner clinic was not owned by a physician, the court held that § 4268 did not apply to them. The court ordered the board to annul the finding of knowing violation of § 4268 and to annul the fine imposed.


OUTCOME: The court annulled the Workers' Compensation Appeals Board's denial of reconsideration and remanded to the board with instructions to annul the finding that petitioners marriage, family, and child counselor and clinic knowingly violated the workers' compensation statute and to annul the civil penalty assessed against petitioners, because petitioner counselor was not a "physician" as defined by the statute.

 

902 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


People v. Samaniego


No. E012531.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


25 Cal. App. 4th 1717; 31 Cal. Rptr. 2d 107; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 623; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4609; 94 Daily Journal DAR 8463



June 17, 1994, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied September 29, 1994 and the Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1994 Cal. LEXIS 5191.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Riverside County, No. ICR-16109, Richard G. Van Frank, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order of the trial court dismissing the subject action after granting defendant's motion pursuant to Penal Code section 1538.5 is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff prosecution appealed an order of the Superior Court of Riverside County (California), which dismissed the case against defendant, charged with possession of heroin for sale in violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11351 and granted defendant's motion pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 1538.5.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, charged with possession of heroin for sale in violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11351, was arrested after his car was stopped for having tinted windows in violation of Cal. Veh. Code § 26708(a). Defendant consented to a search of his vehicle which contained a pager. The officer returned a call from the pager and the caller indicated that she wanted to buy drugs from the defendant. At the time of his arrest no drugs had been found in the car. The trial court granted defendant's Cal. Penal Code § 1538.5 motion and plaintiff prosecution appealed. The court reversed the dismissal order of the trial court because the arresting officer did have probable cause to arrest defendant. The probable cause consisted of drug paraphernalia being found in the car and the caller who paged defendant in order to buy drugs. The court also held that it was permissible to stop a vehicle for having illegal window tinting and the 20-minute investigative detention was proper because the officer was authorized to detain defendant until he completed investigation of the violation and wrote the citation.


OUTCOME: The order of the trial court that dismissed the case against defendant, charged with possession of heroin for sale in violation of Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11351 and granted defendant's motion pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 1538.5 was reversed because the arrest of defendant was supported by probable cause, and the initial stop of his vehicle and the detention that followed were proper.

People v. Schade


No. H009896.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


30 Cal. App. 4th 1515; 32 Cal. Rptr. 2d 59; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 613; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4493; 94 Daily Journal DAR 8273



June 15, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted September 15, 1994 (S040968), Reported at: 1994 Cal. LEXIS 5072.
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cite 25 Cal. App. 4th 1605.)] Review Dismissed May 11, 1995 and cause remanded to the Ct. App., 6th Dist. (rule 29.4(c), Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 3771.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Santa Clara County, No. 139980, James A. Wright, Judge. * 


* Retired judge of the Santa Clara Superior Court sitting under assignment by the Chairperson of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: Appellant's convictions for violating section 11153 are reversed. Appellant's conviction for involuntary manslaughter is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant physician challenged his conviction by the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), of illegal prescription under the Uniform Controlled Substances Act, Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11153 (1982), and of involuntary manslaughter in a patient's suicide, pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 192(b).


OVERVIEW: Appellant physician sought review of his conviction of illegal prescription of a controlled substance under the Uniform Controlled Substances Act, Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11153 (1982), and involuntary manslaughter after a patient's suicide, pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 192(b). The court reversed the illegal prescription conviction because the role of the term "addict" was pivotal in determining whether the conduct met the statutory requirement and the experts could not agree on a definition, and therefore, the trial court, in failing to define it for the jury, committed reversible error. The court affirmed the involuntary manslaughter conviction because there was evidence that appellant's gross negligence and incompetence resulted in the suicide.


OUTCOME: Conviction of a physician for prescribing narcotics in violation of the statute was reversed because the trial court did not define "addict" in the jury charge, but his involuntary manslaughter conviction in the suicide of a patient was affirmed because of his gross negligence and incompetence.

 

904 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


People v. Haywood


No. E010654.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


39 Cal. App. 4th 907; 31 Cal. Rptr. 2d 794; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 589; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4319; 94 Daily Journal DAR 7963



June 9, 1994, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted October 13, 1994 (S041295), Reported at: 1994 1994 Cal. LEXIS 5394.
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cites 25 Cal. App. 4th 1066 and 30 Cal. App. 4th 1087 and 34 Cal. App. 4th 1750.)]
Transferred January 18, 1996 to Ct. App., 4th Dist., Div. 2, with directions to vacate its decision and reconsider in light of People v. Kobin (1995) 11 Cal. 4th 416, Reported at: 1996 Cal. LEXIS 363.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Bernardino County, No. SCR 54931, Patrick J. Morris, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's contentions are meritless. The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of San Bernardino County (California), which convicted him of possession of a firearm by a felon, based on his prior conviction for petty theft with a prior theft conviction under Cal. Penal Code § 666(3). Defendant admitted the priors in the petty theft proceeding and was sentenced to a state prison term, suspended, and placed on probation.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of a firearm by a felon in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 12021(a) and held that defendant was not entitled to an instruction asking the jury to determine whether his prior conviction for petty theft with a prior under Cal. Penal Code § 666(3) was a felony or a misdemeanor. Whether an offense was a felony or a misdemeanor was a question of law to be decided by the court. The trial court correctly determined that defendant's petty theft conviction was for a felony. Defendant was sentenced to the state prison, and his conviction was not a misdemeanor under Cal. Penal Code § 17(b). The court held that defendant was properly sentenced under the indeterminate sentencing law in effect at the time of his trial. The fact that his prison term was suspended and probation granted did not make his petty theft conviction a misdemeanor. Defendant's mistaken belief that he had not been convicted of a felony in the petty theft case was not a defense to the current charge. The court held that defendant voluntarily and knowingly admitted the prior conviction in his previous trial for petty theft and rejected his Yurko error claims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of a firearm by a felon holding that his prior conviction for petty theft with a prior was a felony because he was sentenced to state prison, that determination of whether the petty theft conviction was a felony or misdemeanor was a question of law for the court, and that defendant's mistaken belief that he had not been convicted of a felony was not a defense to the current charge.

 

905 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Beck


No. E011577. , No. E013045.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


25 Cal. App. 4th 1095; 31 Cal. Rptr. 2d 44; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 586; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4316; 94 Daily Journal DAR 7945



June 9, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified June 17, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Bernardino County, No. SCR 54587, Patrick J. Morris, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, convicted of cultivation of marijuana under Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11358, appealed his conviction from the Superior Court of San Bernardino County (California), and filed a petition for writ of mandate to have his firearms that were forfeited under Cal. Penal Code § 12028 returned.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, convicted of cultivation of marijuana under Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11358, was convicted after he reached a plea bargain agreement with prosecution. Following the conviction prosecution sought and received a forfeiture of defendant's firearms under Cal. Penal Code § 12028. Defendant appealed respondent judge's refusal to allow him to withdraw his plea of guilty and filed a petition for writ of mandate to order respondent to issue an order returning defendant's firearms to him. The court reversed respondent's forfeiture order and granted the petition for writ of mandate because the requirements of Cal. Penal Code § 12028 had not been met. The court held that respondent had erred when it held that the firearms could be confiscated without any hearing because the underlying crime to which he pled did not necessarily involve the use of any firearms and the factual basis for the plea did not expressly admit use of any guns. Because the court held that the firearms were improperly confiscated there was no ground upon which defendant could withdraw his plea and his conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The conviction of defendant of cultivation of marijuana, was affirmed because there was no ground upon which defendant could withdraw his plea of guilty. Defendant's petition for writ of mandate was granted because there was no basis for declaring defendant's firearms a nuisance. The order by respondent judge which confiscated defendant's firearms was reversed.

 

906 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



In re Steven S.


No. A060848.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


25 Cal. App. 4th 598; 31 Cal. Rptr. 2d 644; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 546; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 4060; 63 U.S.L.W. 2015; 94 Daily Journal DAR 8155



June 2, 1994, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. *


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with exception of parts IV and V.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied June 28, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 698. Review Denied September 22, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Cal. LEXIS 5185.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Humboldt County, No. 91JV0134, J. Michael Brown, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The jurisdictional and dispositional orders are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the finding of true in the Superior Court of Humboldt County (California), to the allegations that he burned or desecrated a cross on the private property of another for the purpose of terrorizing the owner or occupant or in reckless disregard of that risk.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, purportedly enacting a practical joke, burned a cross on the lawn of an interracial couple. The court held that Cal. Penal Code § 11411 (1982) (statute), did not violate U.S. Const. Amend. I's guarantee of free speech because unauthorized cross burning on another's property was within the scope of the true threat doctrine and the fighting words doctrine. The court did not find the statute overbroad as applied to defendant because, although he claimed he did not intend to terrorize, the true threat doctrine only required intent to perform the act. The court held that the statute did not unlawfully discriminate on the basis of content because the intent of the statute was to protect specific victims from immediate injury, it targeted secondary effects of malicious cross burning, and it was not intended to suppress ideas. The statute was not found to be vague because it required that the offender know the symbolism of the desecrated object and have acted to terrorize or in reckless disregard of the risk. Additionally, the court found no equal protection violation. The court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the finding of true to the allegations that defendant burned or desecrated a cross because the statute making it a crime to burn a cross on the private property of another for the purpose of terrorizing did not violate the First Amendment's guarantee of free speech, did not violate defendant's equal protection rights, and was not vague.

People v. Heilman


No. D019082.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


25 Cal. App. 4th 391; 30 Cal. Rptr. 2d 422; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 519; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3889; 94 Daily Journal DAR 7194



May 27, 1994, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. 1 


1 Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts I and III.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied August 25, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Cal. LEXIS 4596.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, No. CR134876, William H. Kennedy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which convicted him of first degree murder with the use of a firearm under Cal. Penal. Code §§ 187, 189, and 12022.5(a), violating a court order under Cal. Penal. Code § 273.6(a), and stalking under Cal. Penal. Code § 646.9.


OVERVIEW: Defendant convicted of stalking under Cal. Penal Code § 646.9(a) contended that the statute was unconstitutionally vague based on the term "repeatedly" in the statute. The trial court concluded that the statute addressed two behaviors: willful, malicious, repeated following, or willful, malicious harassment. The trial court held that the term "repeatedly" only applied to willful, malicious, repeated following, and therefore, even if it was a vague term, it would not affect defendant's conviction under the willful and malicious harassment provision. The court affirmed, holding that substantial evidence supported defendant's stalking conviction based on a harassment theory, including testimony that he placed unwanted calls to his victim, showed up at her workplace, left threatening notes and wrote threatening messages on her car, appeared at her home and was violent, and damaged her car. The court further held that even if defendant was convicted under the willful, malicious and repeated following provision, his conviction was constitutional because "repeatedly" was a word of such common understanding that its meaning was not vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, holding that substantial evidence supported defendant's stalking conviction based on a harassment theory including testimony that he placed unwanted calls to his victim, showed up at her job, and made threats. The court further held that even if he was convicted under the willful, malicious and repeated following provision of the stalking statute, his conviction was constitutional because the word "repeatedly" was not vague.

Smith v. Fair Employment & Housing Com.


No. C007654.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


39 Cal. App. 4th 877; 30 Cal. Rptr. 2d 395; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 517; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3896; 94 Daily Journal DAR 7223



May 26, 1994, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing June 23, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 649. Review Granted September 8, 1994 (S040653), Reported at: 1994 Cal. LEXIS 4960.
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cites 25 Cal. App. 4th 251 and 30 Cal. App. 4th 1008 and 34 Cal. App. 4th 1708.)] (See 12 Cal. 4th 1143.)



DISPOSITION: Let a writ of mandate issue directing the Commission to vacate its decision and to dismiss the accusation and complaint against plaintiff with prejudice. Plaintiff is to recover her costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landlord appealed from a decision of respondent housing commission (California), which ruled in favor of real parties in interest unmarried couple on a claim of housing discrimination on the basis of marital status.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed the decision of the trial court. Real parties in interest unmarried couple were denied housing by appellant landlord on the basis of their marital status, which would have conflicted with appellant's religious convictions. Respondent housing commission ruled in favor of real parties in interest. On appeal, the court held that the exercise of appellant's U.S. Const. amend. I rights was not precluded by the importance of preventing discrimination based on marital status, which enjoyed a lesser amount of protection than discrimination based on other classifications. The court further held that 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000bb-1 required the application of the compelling state interest test. The court also held that the state constitutional provisions protecting the right to obtain housing and right to privacy were not violated. The court decided that the contention that a state statute prohibiting discrimination by a business establishment had to yield to appellant's paramount right to free exercise and enjoyment of religion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of respondent housing commission on the grounds that appellant landlord's right to exercise and live by her religious convictions outweighed the right not to discriminate against real parties in interest unmarried couple on the basis of marital status.

San Miguel Consolidated Fire Protection Dist. v. Davis


No. C016756.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


25 Cal. App. 4th 134; 30 Cal. Rptr. 2d 343; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 504; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3758; 94 Daily Journal DAR 7004



May 25, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied August 25, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Cal. LEXIS 4606.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sacramento County, No. CV373120, James Timothy Ford, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment (order) is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, fire protection districts and individual taxpayers, sought review from Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which denied their writ of mandate and complaint for declaratory relief against respondents, State Controller, State Director of Finance, and county auditor-controllers. Petitioners challenged the constitutionality of Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 97.03(c), which reallocated a percentage of property tax revenues.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, fire protection districts and individual taxpayers, initiated action for declaratory relief and writ of mandate against respondents, State Controller, State Director of Finance, and county auditor-controllers, and challenged the constitutionality of Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 97.03(c), which reallocated a percentage of property tax revenues from special districts to each county's Educational Revenue Augmentation Fund. The trial court denied petitioners' writ. The court held that petitioners had standing because Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 526a, accorded the individual taxpayers standing. The court held that Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 97.03(c), was not unconstitutionally vague or uncertain. The court determined that Cal. Const. art. XIII A, expressly authorized the legislature to apportion property tax revenues. The court held that the statute did not violate petitioners' equal protection rights because a rational basis existed for the restriction. The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court denying petitioners' writ of mandate and request for declaratory relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, which denied petitioners', fire protection districts and individual taxpayers, writ of mandate and request for declaratory relief against respondents, State Controller, State Director of Finance, and county auditor-controllers. The court held that the challenged statute was constitutional because there was a rational basis for the restriction, which the legislature had authority to implement.

In re Aontae D.


No. D018802.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


25 Cal. App. 4th 167; 30 Cal. Rptr. 2d 176; 1994 Cal. App. LEXIS 479; 94 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3536; 94 Daily Journal DAR 6593



May 16, 1994, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. 1 


1 Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of part III.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, No. 165741, Bonnie Dumanis, Temporary Judge. * 


* Pursuant to California Constitution, article VI, section 21.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile offender appealed a decision from the Superior Court No, 165471of San Diego County (California), which convicted defendant of robbery with the use of a firearm pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 602. Defendant asserted the judge lacked jurisdiction, insufficient evidence to support the findings, and that the trial court erred in refusing to admit polygraph test results in support of defendant's motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant juvenile offender commenced with a friend to rob victim at gunpoint as victim was walking home from work one evening. Victim later identified defendant which led to defendant's arrest and conviction. He was convicted of robbery with the use of a firearm. He asserted that the judge lacked jurisdiction, that there was insufficient evidence to support the findings, and that the trial court erred in refusing to admit polygraph test results in support of a motion for new trial. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court found that the requirement of a written stipulation was directory, and the absence of a writing in this case did not deprive the court of jurisdiction. The court also found sufficient evidence to support the findings. Finally, it concluded that the probative value of the polygraph was insufficient to outweigh the collateral problems of such tests.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court holding the oral stipulation to the judge was sufficient, sufficient evidence to support the findings, and the trial court properly excluded defendant's post trial effort to admit favorable polygraph test results because polygraphs were inherently unreliable or the little probative value garnered from the tests was outweighed by the prejudice and confusion entailed in their introduction.
